Current Commentary

Adhering to Frugality

— Jin

The Third Plenary Session of the Kuomintang passed a motion to vigorously implement the frugality movement. It was decided that the government and the people should work together. Unfortunately, implementation is difficult and the effect is minimal. But we support the frugality movement and will not be discouraged by this. We still advocate saving those materials that are not necessary for daily life and using them as a backup for resisting aggression and saving the country. This is what the authorities and citizens of major countries in the world are working together on. When it comes to the severity of China's national crisis, the exhaustion of its finances, and the poverty of its people's livelihoods, it is probably impossible to find a second country in the world. Logically, we should work harder on frugality in order to accumulate human and material resources to revitalize the country and reverse the current misfortune of the nation. This is a matter of course and falls under the responsibility of citizens, and there is no room for evasion. However, we know that the Chinese people are the most diligent and frugal people in the world, especially the farmers who are engaged in farming. They work hard all year round, putting out the greatest labor and exchanging it for the lowest enjoyment. Their purpose is only to seek a little warmth and food, so they have long been frugal to the point where they cannot be more frugal. Today, we support and advocate frugality, and undoubtedly this is directed at people in large cities and small and medium-sized cities.

China's current poverty is not the responsibility of the rural areas themselves. Because they have already fulfilled their due obligations to the government and the general society. But cities are not the same. Many people among them have not only separated from the group of producers and become pure consumers, but they also often harm the common people and hinder the progress of production. The fact that cities consume material resources and destroy human resources more than rural areas by ten or a hundred times is obvious and can be seen by all. However, since the rural areas have already been exhausted, the impact on the cities must also be very serious. In other words, the urban economy will inevitably gradually move towards bankruptcy due to panic. If there are no effective ways to save it, it may cause the entire national economy to fall into a state of destruction. Although the frugality movement is only one of the ways to save the crisis, if it can be implemented properly, it can also provide considerable assistance.

Now we must ask, from which direction should the frugality movement begin? We believe that it must first start with the political and social leaders themselves. They must make politics clean and honest, and at the same time, they must lead by example and establish a model of a clean and honest government. Those responsible at the central level should set an example for the whole country. Local authorities in each province, and even the county magistrates who are close to the people, should also practice frugality in their respective scopes. If they can truly work for the country and the people, their own enjoyment will not exceed the limits of essential living. After these two points are achieved, they can further use the demeanor they have shown to influence the upper echelons of society. If the upper echelons of society are influenced by them and create a good atmosphere, the result will also affect politics, so that the stains on politics will gradually be washed away. In short, the frugality movement should start from the upper levels, because whether in China or abroad, whether female or male, the people who waste the most and are the most extravagant are always close to the upper class. Therefore, if political leaders and social leaders can truly practice frugality, then more people will follow them. In fact, it is naturally easier to see results.

Speaking of this, we are reminded of the young students of today, because they have a greater possibility of becoming future leaders than ordinary people. Therefore, their behavior is also more closely related to the future of the country and society. There are indeed many young students in the mainland who are able to be frugal and diligent, and who know how to develop the characteristics of an agricultural nation. But there are also quite a few students in cities, especially those above the high school level, who forget their own responsibilities and are immersed in extravagant habits. This is what leaders responsible for political, educational, and social reform should pay special attention to. In short, the frugality movement does not necessarily require it to be universal in all strata of society, but it requires it to achieve the greatest practical effect. Then the mission that the upper class and students should fulfill is particularly great. The reason for this is either because their lives are relatively affluent and they are prone to extravagance, or because their status makes it easy for ordinary people to follow and imitate. The relationship between going out and coming in is extremely great. Whether the frugality movement will repeat the mistakes of the past depends on whether these two groups of people can realize their own mistakes and take action.

Supervisory Yuan Impeaches Gu Mengyu for Illegal Acts and Corruption in the Purchase of Materials for the Datong Road, Should Be Transferred to Disciplinary Action

(Nanjing) Supervisory Committee member Liu Houwu impeached Railway Minister Gu Mengyu for losing national sovereignty, violating national laws, harming national interests, dereliction of duty, and private gain. After the Yuan legally handed it over to committee members Yang Tianji and others for review, it was found that there was no evidence of the alleged loss of sovereignty. However, after reviewing the entire contents of the contract and the procedures for its signing, the minister did engage in illegal acts and corruption, and should be transferred to disciplinary action. The Yuan has prepared the relevant documents and submitted them to the National Government for review and implementation. The original impeachment case and review report, as well as the document submitted to the National Government, were officially announced by the Supervisory Yuan today. (29th Special Dispatch)

Supervisory Yuan's Document to the National Government

(Nanjing) The Supervisory Yuan's document to the National Government stated: "Regarding the submission of the case, according to the impeachment of Railway Minister Gu Mengyu by Supervisory Committee member Liu Houwu for losing national sovereignty, violating national laws, harming national interests, dereliction of duty, and private gain, the case was legally handed over to Supervisory Committee members Yang Tianji, Li Zhengle, and Liu Eqing for review. Now, according to the report, the members reviewed the original impeachment case and found no factual basis for the alleged loss of sovereignty. However, after reviewing the entire contents of the contract and the procedures for its signing, the Railway Minister Gu Mengyu did engage in illegal acts and corruption, and should be transferred to disciplinary action. Based on this, we have prepared the relevant documents and submitted them to your government for review and implementation. Respectfully presented to the Chairman of the National Government, Lin; President of the Supervisory Yuan, Yu Youren."

Review Report

Furthermore, the original review report is as follows. Prior to the review report, it was submitted by the President of the Yuan (院). The case of impeachment against Gu Mengyu, Minister of Railways, by Committee Members Liu and Hou Wu, for relinquishing rights and violating the law, in the matter of the Da-Tong Railway material purchase contract. Upon further review, it was unanimously agreed that the content of the Da-Tong Railway material purchase contract signed by the Ministry of Railways required urgent study. It was requested that the Yuan prepare a document to secretly request the original contract from the ministry for detailed review. Subsequently, Tian Ji, upon instruction, went to the ministry and obtained the contract. After review by the committee members, all opinions are listed as follows: (1) The original impeachment stated that the Ministry of Railways continued to conduct a material loan with Mr. Mardin, the French representative of the Zhengtai Railway, totaling 90 million francs, for the purpose of repairing and extending the Da-Tong Railway. After investigation, the original contract was signed between the Ministry of Railways and the Paris Industrial and Electrical Plant for the purchase of railway materials, with twelve articles. The total price of the materials was 50 million French francs, and the delivery date was sixteen months. Payment for the materials was divided into eleven installments, two installments per year, to be fully paid by January of the 28th year of the Republic. As for the guarantee method, the income of the Zhengtai Railway was designated for payment, and indirectly guaranteed by a consortium of five banks, namely, the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, the Zhongnan Bank, the Jincheng Bank, and the Yanyeh Bank. In addition, the Ministry of Railways signed an engineering advance payment contract and a guaranteed promissory note contract with the banking group, stipulating the date of the bank group's advance payment and the bank group's dispatch of personnel to audit the Zhengtai Railway's income and expenditure, etc. Subsequently, inquiries to the Materials Purchasing Committee of the Ministry claimed that the purchased materials were specifically for the purpose of facilitating the Tongxi section of the Longhai Railway to meet urgent needs, and that the previous plan to build the Da-Tong Railway had been abandoned. Therefore, this contract does not belong to the Da-Tong Railway, and the guarantee part is also indirectly guaranteed by the Chinese banking group, and bank representatives are sent to audit the railway funds. It is also not the creditor's unilateral supervision. Therefore, there is no evidence to support the original impeachment case's claim of relinquishing rights and harming the country.

(2) The original impeachment stated that the amount of this material loan reached 90 million francs. After investigation, the total price of the original contract materials was 50 million French francs. Although it does not match the amount in the impeachment case, after reviewing the entire content of the contract and its signing procedures, the Minister of Railways, Gu Mengyu, did indeed engage in illegal and fraudulent activities. (A) The contract is nominally for material terms, but the type and name of the material are never mentioned. Even the delivery date only states that it will be completed in sixteen months, and it does not specify the amount of each delivery. Conversely, the payment for the materials is listed annually, and an advance promissory note contract is signed with the Chinese banking group as an attachment. Therefore, the content is purely in the form of a loan contract. The minister used the name of purchasing materials as a disguised loan, hoping to deceive the people of the country and avoid the review procedures of the Legislative Yuan, and secretly signed it. This is the first instance of illegal and fraudulent activities. (B) The contract was signed on March 6th of the 22nd year of the Republic, and the two attached contracts with the banking group were signed on July 1st of the same year. It was only after the Yuan had filed an impeachment on May 7th of this year and retrieved the original contract that it was reported to the Executive Yuan meeting (see the minutes of the 159th meeting of the Executive Yuan). This is the second instance of illegal and fraudulent activities because it was not reported to the Executive Yuan for approval beforehand, which does not comply with administrative legal procedures. (C) According to the Provisional Regulations for Material Purchase of the Ministry of Railways, all material purchases above 5,000 yuan must be put out to tender to prevent favoritism and fraud. The total amount of material purchase in the original contract was 50 million francs, equivalent to more than 10 million yuan in national currency. Why was the contract not signed secretly with the so-called Paris Industrial and Electrical Plant without going through open bidding procedures? This is the third instance of illegal and fraudulent activities. Based on the above points, the impeached person, Minister of Railways, Gu Mengyu, should be transferred to the Disciplinary Committee in accordance with the law to warn against private interests and maintain the rule of law. Respectfully submitted to the President of the Yuan. Yang Tianji, Li Zhengle, Liu Eqing.

Original Text of the Impeachment Case

Furthermore, Supervisory Committee Members Liu and Hou Wu submitted a document to the President of the Yuan stating: "Submitting a proposal for impeachment. The procedures for the country to borrow foreign funds are very detailed, and the government's planning for railway construction should be especially cautious. The Ministry of Railways, as the highest administrative authority in charge of national roads, should respect national sovereignty when utilizing foreign capital, avoid being bound by harsh conditions, and comply with national laws. It should submit proposals to the Central Political Conference for approval and then to the Legislative Yuan for review before implementation. Route construction should develop the future interests of the country and the people with the most economical policies, eliminating all the old corruption of inflated costs and embezzlement. The responsibility is self-evident. However, the current Minister of Railways, Gu Mengyu, has made a serious mistake in handling the material loan for the Da-Tong Railway. An investigation reveals four aspects of his actions that relinquish rights, violate the law, harm the country, and serve private interests, which are listed as follows:"

"(1) The Zhengtai Railway originally borrowed 40 million French francs, with a term of 30 years, and the principal and interest were paid back on schedule. As of March 1st of the 21st year of the Republic, the debt had been fully repaid. According to the contract, the contract should have been terminated and the railway taken back for independent operation. However, Gu Mengyu delayed the takeover and secretly continued a material loan with Mr. Mardin, the French representative (i.e., the French side purchases materials on behalf and settles accounts as cash, which is repaid in installments every six months for ten installments). After Mr. Mardin returned to France, he signed a material loan agreement with a Paris electrical manufacturer for a total of 90 million French francs for the expansion and repair of the Da-Tong Railway, divided into three batches: 50 million French francs in the first batch, 25 million French francs in the second batch, and 15 million French francs in the third batch. A separate contract was signed for each batch. On July 1st of the 22nd year of the Republic, Gu Mengyu sent representatives to sign the agreement with the representatives of the Paris electrical manufacturer, causing the formal takeover of the Zhengtai Railway to be delayed by as much as one year. Fearing criticism from foreigners, the material loan contract was falsely called a material purchase contract (it is said that several batches of the materials have arrived and are being used for the Tongxi section of the Longhai Railway and the Da-Tong Railway). This material loan is secured by the income of the newly taken-over Zhengtai Railway, and also guaranteed by the Bank of China and other Chinese bank groups. In addition, Mr. Vinot, a French national, continues to serve as the head of the Traffic Department of the Zhengtai Railway, and Mr. Boyan, a French national, is appointed as the chief auditor of the Zhengtai Railway and the chief engineer of the Da-Tong Railway. Due to debt relations, the China Communications and other bank groups have also dispatched Wang Yizeng, the president of the Shijiazhuang Bank of Communications, as a resident supervisor. It appears that the Zhengtai Railway is taken over in name only, and the major power is still controlled by French nationals. All income is used as an unlimited guarantee, and the conditions are particularly harsh. This is the minister's disregard for the interests of the country in borrowing foreign funds and the loss of national sovereignty, for which he should be punished."

"(2) The amount of this material loan reaches 90 million French francs. Since it is nominally for the expansion and repair of the Da-Tong Railway, and it is known that the uneconomical construction funds and the harsh conditions that damage national sovereignty cannot obtain the consent of the Central Political Conference and the legislative bodies. Therefore, on the surface, it is called a material purchase loan, divided into batches and contracted for small amounts, hoping to deceive the people of the country and avoid the legal procedures of submitting a request to the Central Political Conference for approval and submitting it to the Legislative Yuan for review in accordance with the law. This is the minister's violation of national law and his skillful evasion of the exercise of the powers of the Central Political Conference and the legislative bodies, for which he should be punished."

"(3) The so-called Da-Tong line has been under construction for almost a year. Only 35 kilometers of the original earthwork have been repaired from Yuci along the old Tongcheng line to Taigu, and only five or six miles of track have been laid (the track gauge is four feet eight and a half inches, which is narrower than the Zhengtai Railway's gauge of one meter). The Tongpu Railway built by the Shanxi arsenal also starts from Taiyuan, passing through Lunci Taigu to Jiexiu. The Zhengtai Railway between Taiyuan and Yuci and the Da-Tong Railway between Yuci and Taigu face each other from a distance, both becoming parallel lines at the closest distance. At a time when the state-owned railway is in urgent need of expansion, there are more important domestic transportation routes that need to be built than this one. The minister borrowed a huge amount of foreign capital, but only for the construction of this parallel route, giving priority to what is slow and neglecting what is important. His understanding of the overall situation is poor, and his measures are misguided. Moreover, during the current construction period, he is wasting time and wasting salaries. Even if the route is fortunately completed in the future, it will lead to business competition due to the two parallel routes, and the result will inevitably lead to two failures. This is the minister's improper measures and deliberate damage to the country's interests, for which he should be punished."

"(4) Article 136 of the Criminal Law on dereliction of duty states that a public official who directly or indirectly seeks personal gain from matters under his jurisdiction or supervision shall be sentenced to imprisonment for up to three years and may also be fined up to three thousand yuan. Now, the minister has secretly carried out this huge material loan without going through legal procedures. He has fabricated names and falsely called it a material purchase contract. He has even disregarded the ordinary procedures for government agencies to openly bid for the purchase of goods. May I ask, can the eyes and ears of the 400 million people be completely covered up by the purchase of 90 million francs of materials, which is a huge sum of money? Some say that there are many shady deals in this material purchase, and the ingenuity of its profiteering and the amount of embezzlement are even greater than the loan rebates during the era of the Beijing government. People are talking about it, and it is not without reason. At a time when the world economy is depressed and the supply of goods from various countries exceeds demand, and the devaluation and competitive sale of goods has become a common phenomenon, there is no standard for the quality, price, and value of the materials purchased by the French side. The contract was secretly signed beforehand, and it was kept secret. Afterwards, there was no formal open bidding. Who would believe that he was not seeking personal gain? This is the minister's dereliction of duty and pursuit of personal gain, for which he should be punished."

"In summary, the above-mentioned points clearly show that the Minister of Railways, Gu Mengyu, has relinquished national sovereignty, violated national laws, damaged national interests, and committed dereliction of duty and pursuit of personal gain. He should be severely punished. Now, in accordance with the law, I hereby propose an impeachment and respectfully request that it be transferred to the Disciplinary Committee to uphold national law and warn against official corruption, which is in the public interest. Respectfully submitted to the President of the Yuan. (Including one drawing) Supervisory Committee Member Liu Houwu. (29th Daily Telegram)"

President Roosevelt Declares a New Beginning with the People, Implementing Three Major Tasks for the Benefit of the People, Denies Communism or Fascism, and the Achievements of the Recovery Have Not Damaged Constitutional Rights

(Washington) President Roosevelt gave a radio address to the nation tonight, saying that the government's greatest goal is to restore basic fairness and justice, and strongly denied any communist or fascist tendencies. The President also described his achievements, saying that the government's most important goals in the future are three: (1) Economic security for every American citizen, (2) Developing America's land and water resources, (3) Social insurance. The President did not elaborate on how the government will achieve these goals, but said that he will be able to provide a detailed explanation to the people of the country in the future. Roosevelt praised Congress's achievements and recognized the elimination of partisan prejudices as the greatest success because it was able to discuss everything in an impartial and non-partisan spirit. The President then briefly described the proceedings of the last Congress and paid special attention to Mr. Vincent's most advantageous naval bill and the newly established monetary system. Roosevelt said, "The most important success of Congress is the establishment of policies suitable for modern life, making the American monetary system more equitable, and making gold and silver both the basis of the American monetary system." The President then compared his policies with those of previous presidents in the past ten years, believing that they were all too short-sighted. Therefore, when he took office in March 1933, he implemented the following three plans: (1) Relief for unemployment and poverty, (2) Economic recovery, (3) Improving the adverse conditions caused by the economic decline and restoring basic justice and fairness. Since the implementation of this plan, the number of unemployed has been greatly reduced, rural income has increased sharply, and all businesses have gradually returned to normal. As for the critics who said that his policies are not in line with the traditional American norms, Roosevelt retorted, saying, "I ask, who has lost their rights and freedoms within the scope of the Constitution?" The President believes that those who generally believe that they have been harmed by the New Deal are all those who demand special political and financial rights. They are all complaining because they cannot harm others for their own benefit by means of ingenuity. The President said that the ruling power of the people has gradually restored confidence in the country, so there is no need to overthink that the New Deal has communist and fascist tendencies. Finally, Roosevelt briefly described his plan to tour Honolulu, which will be held with Haiti Colombia and Panama president meeting said. (28th National Telegram)

(Washington) President Luo broadcast an address to the nation today for the first time since last October, summarizing the achievements of the authorities' recovery movement. He said: "Today, there are four things, and I ask the people to answer: (1) Is your current life better than last year? (2) Are your debt burdens lighter than before? (3) Are your bank deposits safer than before? (4) Has your work situation improved compared to before? What are your answers? There is no doubt that the three steps the government is currently taking to protect the national life are relief, recovery, and aftercare. These steps are necessary for three reasons: One is the depression caused by the Chinese people's狂妄 pursuit of unearned wealth in the past ten years, two is that many of today's difficulties are caused by the business and financial leaders' ignorance of the basic principles of fairness and justice, and three are the new conditions in the economic life." President Luo then mentioned the increase in wages, the reduction in unemployment, the increase in the value of agricultural products, and the exemption of thousands of families from displacement, pointing to this as clear evidence of the success of his policies, and said that the government has achieved this result without harming the rights of freedom under the Constitution. Although some people feel inconvenienced, they are only a minority in comparison. In the future, the government will devote itself to better housing, the use of land and water resources, and the establishment of social insurance in the people's livelihood security program. President Luo also mentioned industrial autonomy, saying that the purpose of our construction is to protect industries from fighting each other, and to protect consumers and maintain appropriate competition to avoid the crazy rise of retail prices. A few cowards who are worried about progress often want to 䨓 with strange terms such as fascism, communism or socialism etc., in fact, what we do is very simple, and in line with implementation, it is just that the average coward wants to make it complicated. We are now implementing the ideals inherent in the United States that have been tried and tested. Other countries may sacrifice democracy and want to seek transitional excitement in corrupt and discredited dictatorships, but we want to restore the credibility and welfare of democracy. President Luo finally mentioned the work of Congress, the most important event that Congress has already passed, for the change of the monetary system, the establishment of new life standards, and the treatment of gold and silver fairly, considering them as the base of American currency. (28th Reuters Telegram)

The U.S. Treasury Department Announces a Ban on Silver Exports to Prevent Speculators from Profiteering, and Severe Penalties for Those Who Violate It

(Washington) Today, the U.S. government suddenly announced a ban on silver exports. Experts here believe that this is aimed at silver speculators. After the ban is issued, speculators will not be able to ship silver out of the United States and buy it back from the United States in foreign markets, thus circumventing the 50% profit tax. This ban was issued by Treasury Secretary Morganthau and is roughly the same as last year's ban on gold exports. However, exported silver that was traded before the ban was issued can still be shipped out with a license. In addition, manufactured goods made of silver are not subject to the ban. To obtain an export license, the following evidence must be submitted to the Treasury Department: (1) The silver to be shipped is to fulfill a contract signed before the ban was issued; (2) The silver has been owned by a foreign government, foreign bank, or international clearing bank recognized by the United States before the ban was issued; (3) It is a transit cargo or delivered to a metallurgical plant for refining; (4) Alloy silver with less than 80% purity; (5) Permitted by the President and not in conflict with the Silver Law of 1934. Those who violate it will be fined up to 10,000 yuan or imprisoned for up to ten years. (28th National Telegram)

(London) New York recently sold US dollars in anticipation that President Luo's speech would contain a preview of currency inflation. However, President Luo's speech has now been delivered, and this hope has become a bubble. Therefore, the sale of US dollars may stop. Former French Finance Minister Renault's remarks in the House of Representatives, pointing out the difficulties currently encountered by French industries and the difference between French prices and world prices, as well as the recent disturbances in various provinces of France, are now causing concerns about the future of the franc. Parisian funds are now gradually flowing into London, and this trend is promoted by the British government's control of the exchange market. However, London Financial News does not approve of this move by the British government, saying that the British Exchange Equalization Fund is gradually running out of money and a lot of gold has been consumed. It should now allow the franc to rise and fall on its own in order to preserve the equalization fund for future protection of the pound. However, other parties currently believe that the current price of Continental gold coins converted into pounds is too high. (29th Reuters Telegram)

(Washington) National Bank officials announced today that bank deposits have increased by approximately US$10 billion since February. The increase in deposits in mid-April has never exceeded this number. Moreover, this increase does not include the government's sharply increased deposits, nor does it include the deposits of other banks. Therefore, this increase is sufficient to represent the savings of individuals and companies. Officials here unanimously expressed optimism about the sharp increase in bank deposits. They not only regard this as a restoration of the American people's belief in banks, but also regard this as a sign of progress in recovery work. (28th National Telegram)

British Economist

On China and Silver Prices

(London) A memorandum from Manchester today contains an article by the renowned economist Sir Charles, roughly stating that it is regrettable that China's power has not been used effectively. What China needs is the stability of silver prices, not artificial increases. China's interests should allow it to have a dominant influence in silver policy. China was uniquely able to avoid the world economic misfortunes of 1930 and 1931 because of the low silver prices. Since Japan and the United States abandoned the gold standard, silver prices have risen sharply, and the situation has changed. China's exports have greatly decreased, leading to a serious trade deficit and the need for capital outflow. Due to internal unrest, silver is now concentrated in Shanghai, which exacerbates the difficulties, while the interior lacks currency and prices are falling. China must restore its original internal situation so that foreign capital can flow back into China. (28th Reuters)

British Revision of Silk Tariffs: Major Impact on Our Country's Exports

(London) The British Treasury issued an order today, announcing revised tariffs on natural silk, rayon, and goods made entirely or partially from natural silk or rayon, effective July 2nd. Eastern silks, such as those produced in Shandong, Ninghai, Nanshan, Henan, Andong, and Khabartai, will be taxed at three shillings and sixpence for dyed and printed varieties, and two shillings and ninepence for undyed and unprinted varieties. Furthermore, the above-mentioned Eastern silks, if dyed or printed, will also be subject to a tax of 25% of the value of the goods, or an additional seven and a half pence per square yard. In addition, the tax rate for goods made entirely or partially from natural silk or rayon will remain unchanged unless the natural silk or rayon content exceeds 5% of the value of the goods, but if the value does not exceed 20% of the total value of the various components of the goods, the tax rate will increase by 20% to 25%. (28th Reuters)

(London) Today, a Reuters reporter visited personnel from the Silk Association to inquire about the impact of the new Anglo-French commercial treaty. The response was that they had not yet fully studied the document, but they believed that it would have a significant impact on Chinese silk. Any benefits gained from the low tax rate on dyed and printed silks would be entirely offset by the increased tax rate on unprinted and undyed silks. The number of printed and dyed silks imported by Britain from China is very small. The Silk Association is quite impatient with the government's delay in resolving this issue and will hold an important meeting next week. Currently, there are no apparent negotiations between Britain and Japan on this matter. (29th Reuters)

Contents of the Anglo-French Commercial Treaty

(London) The Anglo-French commercial treaty signed yesterday stipulates that the two countries will grant each other most-favored-nation status. France will restore the original quotas for British goods, Britain will abolish the 20% duty on French goods, France will maintain the current percentage of British coal imports, and Britain will also revise import duties on silk, reducing the current tax rate on raw silk by half and re-examining the tax rate on silk goods to slightly increase the import tax on silk goods. It is estimated that this revision will reduce the British treasury's revenue by three million pounds per year. The Anglo-French commercial treaty is valid until April 1, 1935. During the validity of this treaty, Britain will not increase import duties on French brandy and other alcoholic beverages. After the treaty expires, taxes may be increased, but three months' notice must be given in advance. (28th Reuters)

(Washington) Negotiations in Moscow on the repayment of Russian debts to the United States have reached a stalemate. It is expected that the U.S.-Russian negotiations will be transferred to Washington for handling. U.S. officials believe that the atmosphere in Washington will be more conducive to negotiations, but those close to the negotiators say that a resolution may not be reached before this autumn. It is rumored that progress has been made on the principal amount to be repaid, but serious disputes have arisen over the interest rate and payment method. (29th Reuters)

U.S. Note to Germany: Dissatisfaction with Explanation of Debt Suspension; Says Germany's Inability to Pay Debts is Self-Inflicted

(Washington) Secretary of State Hull today sent a very blunt note to the German government, calling its recent explanation for the suspension of war debt payments "highly inappropriate." The note stated that Germany's explanation was simply an attempt to hold creditor nations responsible for the debtor nation's inability to fulfill its obligations due to poor business conditions. As for Germany's difficulties, the United States believes that political factors are largely responsible, which has hindered trade, and foreign capital in Germany is gradually being withdrawn. Moreover, foreigners are aware that Germany is using commercial surpluses to buy back its own bonds in foreign markets at low prices and to purchase military equipment, while neglecting its debt obligations. If Germany wanted to fulfill its debt obligations, it could simply attribute it to poor business performance. Although the United States does not wish to express an opinion on the impact of the suspension of payments on the Dawes and Young plans because it is not a signatory country, it opposes any discriminatory treatment of U.S. bondholders. The final draft of the constitution was announced today in the capital of Brazil, specifically prohibiting Japanese immigration to Brazil. The new constitution limits the number of immigrants from any country to 2% of the total number of residents from that country in the past 50 years. Therefore, once the new constitution is approved, it will ban Japanese immigration. In the past 30 years, a total of 150,000 Japanese immigrants have come to Brazil. The number has increased dramatically in recent years, reaching 10,000 in the past year alone. Under the new constitution, the number of Japanese immigrants must be reduced to 3,000 per year. British Labour Party Changes Anti-War Stance: Says There is a Difference Between Aggression and Peacekeeping in the Same War

(London) The leaders of the British Trades Union Congress and the Labour Party met today to consider the motion passed by the Labour Party Congress last year to declare a general strike in the event of war. As a result, the meeting abandoned its resolute opposition to any war and decided on a declaration stating that a distinction must be made between wars of aggression and wars to safeguard peace. British Labour resolutely opposes any war of aggression, but Britain may encounter special circumstances where it has no choice but to resort to force to maintain the League of Nations and stop aggressor nations. This declaration will be submitted to the next congress of the Trades Union Congress and the Labour Party. The Labour Party newspaper welcomed the declaration, saying that it would strengthen the collective guarantee of peace. (29th Reuters)

Disarmament Lifeless: Discussions on Safeguards and Sanctions Useless; Second Committee Can Only Adjourn

(Geneva) The Second Committee of the Disarmament Commission, which was formed on the 11th of this month in accordance with the compromise plan of French Foreign Minister Barthou and tasked with discussing the implementation, safeguards, and supervision of the future disarmament convention, met today under the chairmanship of the Belgian representative, Pulgan, to study the draft classification of safeguards and sanctions proposed by the chairman. The main purpose of the draft is to classify the violation and sanction methods to ensure that they are rigid, while the wording of the classification content may be slightly flexible. Any violation, depending on the severity of the circumstances, will be certified by the regional committee once discovered by the League of Nations or the Permanent Disarmament Commission. The nature of the violation is extremely serious and constitutes a danger of aggression, which is a political issue and should be intervened by the League of Nations together with the governments of the countries concerned. As Barthou Passes Through, Austria Sees New Terrorist Acts: Bombs Destroy Railroad Tracks at Night; Water Pipes Burst, Almost Creating a Swamp

The outbreak of the second bombing wave in Vienna reached its peak in Upper Austria this morning, and the Dollfuss cabinet, threatened by this, had to convene an emergency meeting this afternoon. Among the various bombing incidents, the most alarming was the destruction of three sections of the scenic railway between Innsbruck and Kapl. The railroad tracks near Bludenz were blasted into the air. French Foreign Minister Barthou had just passed through there an hour before on his way back to Paris from Belgrade. Other important railways that were destroyed were one in Styria and one in the suburbs of Lower Austria's Salzburg. The perpetrators of the above bombing incidents were well-planned and completely successful. Telephones and electrical wires in the surrounding areas were also cut in advance or after the fact. Furthermore, the most shocking of the bombing incidents last night was the explosion of a high-pressure water pipe in Constanz. The water pipe was buried on the mountain, so the villages below the mountain were awakened in the middle of the night. At the same time, large amounts of iron and stone flew around and fell on the houses in the village. After the water pipe burst, floods broke out, turning the cliffs into swamps. In Innsbruck, a night watchman at a newspaper office found a suspicious-looking package on the roof. He picked it up and threw it into the garden of a nearby hotel, but the object exploded immediately, destroying the entire hotel and shattering the windows of the newspaper building. (Fuzhou) The organization of the various security regiments into divisions will be decided after Xiao Qian returns to Fujian. Xiao and Wang Jinxiu, the garrison commander of the Min River, will both be appointed as division commanders. (29th Special Dispatch)

Hangzhou Suffering from Extreme Heat and Worries about Drought

(Hangzhou) The heat here is severe, with the temperature remaining high for days without relief. The paddy fields in the West Lake area and the four rural areas of Hangzhou are showing signs of drought. It is reported that the authorities are considering opening the lake gates to provide relief. Various counties are also eagerly awaiting rain. Furthermore, the epidemic in Hangzhou is increasing. (29th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Zhenjiang) At the Jiangsu Provincial Government's regular meeting on the 29th, the following resolutions were passed: 1. (29th Special Dispatch)

Announcement of the Beiping-Shenyang Through Train Plan - Beiping-Liaoning Railway Assigns Personnel to Serve the Through Train - The Oriental Travel Agency Decides to Operate in Three Departments

Beiping Correspondence: The resumption of the Beiping-Shenyang through train service was announced simultaneously by both Chinese and Japanese sides today (the 28th) in the morning. On the Beiping side, the Beiping-Liaoning Railway Bureau specially dispatched Wu Songhua, a member of the Bureau's Improvement Committee and former Deputy Director of the General Affairs Department, carrying the announcement documents. He arrived in Beiping from Tianjin on the Beiping-Liaoning Railway's 10th train at 11:20 PM last night. At 8:00 AM this morning, the announcement was made at the Bureau's Beiping Office at Qianmen Station. However, what was announced was not the so-called "Through Train Plan," but only a "Notice on the Resumption of Through Passenger Train Service between Beiping and Shenyang" and "Special Express Train Passenger Instructions" issued in the name of Director Yin Tong. On the Japanese side, Military Attaché Chiba of the Japanese Embassy announced it at 8:00 AM in the military attaché's office. The content was the same as the "Notice" from the Beiping-Liaoning Railway. Chiba also released a statement in his personal capacity on his thoughts on the resumption of through train service, which was published in both English and Japanese. Due to the impending commencement of service on July 1, the Beiping-Liaoning Railway Bureau has assigned all personnel to serve on the through train, including 15 train conductors, train guards, and ticket inspectors, who will be divided into three shifts to serve in rotation. The train conductors assigned were Pang Jiaqin, Zhou Dechang, and Chen Tiqiang. The train used for the Beiping-Shenyang through service was driven from Fengtai to Tianjin yesterday for a test run. It is scheduled to return tomorrow (29th) and will depart from Qianmen on the evening of the 30th to travel to Shenyang on the first. Zhang Shuiqi, nominated by the China Travel Service to serve as the general manager of the Oriental Travel Agency, previously went to Yu Pass with four important staff members of the agency to negotiate and sign a contract with representatives from the Japanese South Manchuria Railway and the Tourist Bureau to jointly establish the Oriental Travel Agency. Except for the train schedule and ticket revenue settlement issues, all matters were negotiated and resolved. Both parties signed the contract in Yu Pass on the 27th and agreed that the Japanese side would relinquish part of the Beiping-Liaoning Railway buildings near the Yu Pass Station occupied by the Japanese army for use as the headquarters of the Oriental Travel Agency. Zhang Shuiqi returned to Tianjin from Yu Pass on the Beiping-Liaoning Railway's 8th train at 2:00 PM yesterday. Today, he will continue to work with representatives from the Beiping-Liaoning Railway Bureau and the Japanese side in Tianjin to negotiate and finalize issues such as the train schedule and ticket revenue settlement. Chen Xiangtao, the general manager of the China Travel Service, also took the Beiping-Liaoning Railway's 9th passenger train from Beiping to Tianjin at 2:25 PM this afternoon to participate in the negotiations. It is expected that everything will be completed today. The train schedule will be finalized today and will be sent to the China Travel Service, the Japanese International Tourist Bureau, and the Tongjilong Transportation Company for them to start selling tickets from July 1. The tickets are in two parts. When passing through Yu Pass, one part is torn off and kept by the Oriental Travel Agency for reference, and the remainder is given to the passenger to keep. When arriving at the final station, the railway bureau collects it for verification.

Chiba Releases Statement

Military Attaché Chiba of the Japanese Embassy released a statement today (the 28th) regarding his thoughts on the through train service. The English original is translated as follows: "The successful resolution of the through train issue is truly a cause for celebration for both China and Japan. This issue was a local and technical matter and should have been resolved sooner. However, due to the limitations of the complex environment, it was delayed until today. I do not wish to discuss the reasons for this. I sincerely hope that the resolution of the through train issue will be a precursor to increased friendly relations between China and Japan. Therefore, I am very pleased with the implementation of the through train service."

Beiping-Liaoning Railway Bureau Notice

Notice from the Beiping-Liaoning Railway Administration: "Regarding the issue of passenger trains passing between inside and outside the Pass, the Executive Yuan's Beiping Political Affairs Reorganization Committee previously forwarded the Executive Yuan's order to negotiate with Japanese representatives based on the standards approved by the Premier of the Executive Yuan and the Chairman of the Military Affairs Commission. After carrying out negotiations and agreeing on specific measures, it has been submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval and filing. It has now been decided to implement the measures from July 1. The measures are hereby announced as follows: 1. Starting from July 1 of this year, through passenger trains from Beiping to Liaoning will be restored, limited to one round trip per day between Beiping and Shenyang. 2. The Chinese side will be responsible for the China Travel Service, and the Japanese side will be responsible for the Japanese Tourist Bureau to jointly establish the Oriental Travel Agency in Shanhaiguan to manage the through train service. 3. All operating regulations, schedules, train formation, ticket sales, and other measures will be separately stipulated by the Railway Bureau. Director Yin Tong, June 28, 23rd year of the Republic of China."

Process of Determining the Name

During the meeting in Tianjin, it was decided with the agreement of both parties to name it the "Oriental Travel Agency." After the name was decided, four requirements were raised: 1. The Oriental Travel Agency should be registered in China and should comply with Chinese laws. 2. The general manager of the Oriental Travel Agency will always be Chinese. 3. The Oriental Travel Agency will only be related to the Beiping-Liaoning Railway, the Japanese Tourist Bureau, and the South Manchuria Railway, and will not conduct negotiations with any other third parties. 4. The selection of the general manager and deputy manager will be determined by the Chinese and Japanese sides respectively. After discussion, the Japanese side agreed to all the requests. The Tianjin meeting then came to an end.

Organization of the Travel Agency

The capital of the Oriental Travel Agency is set at one million yuan, with the China Travel Service and the Japanese International Tourist Bureau each contributing half. Both parties will designate banks to store the funds as a guarantee for train safety. The agency's expenses will only be covered by the 5% commission from the first, second, and third class passenger tickets sold for the Beiping-Shenyang through train service. If this is not enough, the railway bureau will subsidize the agency. The agency's headquarters will be located in Yu Pass, and no branch offices will be established. Ticket sales inside and outside the Pass will be handled separately by major stations and the China Travel Service and the Japanese International Tourist Bureau. Train operations will be the responsibility of the stations in each section inside and outside the Pass. The internal organization of the travel agency will be divided into four departments: 1. Documentation Department: responsible for transmitting official documents and compiling schedules. 2. Accounting Department: responsible for currency conversion between Chinese and Japanese systems and ticket revenue statistics. 3. General Affairs Department: responsible for all administrative affairs. 4. Sales Department: responsible for sales matters, and Zhang Shuiqi, a director of the China Travel Service, will be appointed as the general manager of the Oriental Travel Agency.

Contract Signed in Yu Pass

After the Tianjin meeting, Zhang Shuiqi, a director of the China Travel Service, and four others traveled to Yu Pass the day before yesterday to negotiate issues related to the through train service and sign the contract. The most important issue discussed in Yu Pass was the settlement issue. Since both sides have the same number of service personnel, capital, and stations inside and outside the Pass, both sides should collect ticket revenue separately, without the need for settlement procedures. The Japanese side has not yet agreed to this, using the universal postal system as an example. In addition, the procedures for inspecting the carriages passing through Yu Pass also need to be negotiated. The Japanese side has sent Adachi, a representative from the South Manchuria Railway, to Yu Pass to discuss all matters. It will not be difficult to reach a decision. The announcement of the plan today and the implementation of the through train service on July 1 will not be delayed as a result.

Mr. Chen Xiangtao Discusses Solutions

Chen Xiangtao, the general manager of China Travel Service, discussed the case of operating passenger trains between Beiping and Shenyang, stating that the government decided to have a commercial organization handle it. Among domestic travel businesses independently operated by Chinese with proven success, China Travel Service was the only one. The government instructed the company to jointly establish the Oriental Travel Service with the Japan Tourist Bureau to handle special express train services, with a Chinese national serving as the general manager. After receiving an official letter from the Ministry of Railways, China Travel Service initially hesitated to take on the task, but the government's urging made it difficult to refuse. From the perspective of the nation, especially during times of national crisis, they felt compelled to contribute their efforts. Therefore, the company's board of directors held repeated meetings and finally decided to comply with the government's order and undertake the Oriental Travel Service project. Once the Oriental Travel Service is established, significant expenses are anticipated. It is rumored that the allocated funds, consisting of only five percent commission from railway ticket sales, will be insufficient. However, China Travel Service views this matter as serving the nation and the people inside and outside the Great Wall, and they will not hesitate to bear any losses.

Unscrupulous Merchants Seize Opportunity to Profit

With the imminent opening of through train service between Beiping and Shenyang, unscrupulous merchants in Beiping are transporting copper coins into the country, hoping to profit. The Bureau of Social Affairs sent a letter to the Bureaus of Finance and Public Safety, requesting them to dispatch representatives to discuss methods to prevent this, in order to maintain financial stability. The original letter is as follows: "Upon investigation, the price of copper coins in our city plummeted after last year's sharp decline. The Municipal Government repeatedly ordered this bureau to work with your bureau and the Bureaus of Finance (and Public Safety) to take strict measures. Representatives from the three bureaus and the Chamber of Commerce were dispatched daily to the money market to set exchange rate standards for restriction. However, recently, the puppet regime revised the currency system, effective June 1st, prohibiting the sale and circulation of copper coins, with violators being charged with disrupting the financial order. Unscrupulous merchants are taking advantage of this opportunity to buy up large quantities of copper coins and transport them into the country as much as possible. As a result, the amount of copper coins in the country has skyrocketed, and the price has plummeted. Currently, in Tianjin, Yangcun, Tangshan, and other places, each yuan can be exchanged for as many as 580 to 600 copper coins. Copper coins are everywhere, but commodity prices are calculated in silver yuan, causing small vendors and laborers to complain incessantly. Although the price of copper coins in our city is under strict surveillance, it is still falling daily. Currently, each yuan can be exchanged for 525 or 526 copper coins. The previous stability has gradually been shaken. This not only affects the livelihood of ordinary people but also impacts the overall economic situation of our city. If measures are not taken early, the future is worrisome. Once the through train service is realized, it will be even more difficult to prevent, which is especially concerning. Now, it is proposed to follow the Municipal Government's previous order and reconvene a meeting to discuss methods to restrict the decline in the price of copper coins, in order to uphold the law and maintain the people's livelihood. Besides sending separate letters, this letter is sent for your review and to request that you dispatch representatives to jointly discuss the matter." (28th)

Amidst Intense Bandit Suppression, Sichuan Province Strives for New Initiatives, Liu Xiang Convenes Subordinates to Give Instructions and Announce Regulations, Establishes New Life Movement Group and Use of Domestic Goods Association

Chengdu Airmail: The issue of bandit suppression in Sichuan Province has progressed rapidly since the capture of Tongcheng. Currently, the Five Route Army is exerting all its efforts to fiercely attack the bandit gangs in Wanyuan. The First, Second, Third, Fourth, and Sixth Routes have all been ordered to coordinate their attacks, and the military situation has suddenly become more tense than before. At this time, the New Life Movement in Chengdu and Chongqing is also being vigorously promoted. The Governor's and Commander's Headquarters have recently established organizations such as the New Life Movement Group and the Use of Domestic Goods Committee. Yesterday, Liu Xiang convened a meeting of staff, including Chief of Staff Li Jianming, Secretary-General Zhang Biguo, and more than one hundred others. Liu gave important instructions, roughly stating: "Since the establishment of this headquarters in the province, it has been almost a year. Due to the complexity of affairs, I have not had the opportunity to convene a meeting for discussion. Today, as we gather together, I would like to propose two matters for your consideration: one is the organization of the New Life Movement Group in this headquarters, and the other is the establishment of the Use of Domestic Goods Committee in this headquarters. Although these two matters are clearly separate, their ultimate goal is to achieve the purpose of saving the country and benefiting the people. Currently, the national crisis is severe, the economy is bankrupt, and the general public is accustomed to extravagance. Living habits are all unreasonable. If this continues, the Chinese nation will fall into an incurable state. Chairman Chiang cannot bear to see our inherent virtues disappear, so he initiated the New Life Movement. The whole country responded enthusiastically, and the atmosphere has been renewed. Chengdu and Chongqing have also gradually promoted it. In fact, the essence of the New Life Movement, such as filial piety, brotherly love, loyalty, trustworthiness, propriety, righteousness, integrity, and a sense of shame, as well as diligence, frugality, and simplicity, are all inherent good habits. The reason for naming it the New Life Movement is merely that these virtues and good practices have long disappeared and need to be restored. These regulations are all simple and easy to implement. If we can all persevere, then once habits are formed, any difficulties can be overcome. This headquarters is a high-level administrative organ, and the lives and actions of all staff members can influence society. If we do not strive to implement the New Life Movement, then the general bad habits will be difficult to change. However, the regulations of the New Life Movement Group organized by this headquarters this time are based on complete implementation. Therefore, you must carefully consider when seeking opinions, and if you feel that you cannot implement them, do not force yourself to join, so as not to become an obstacle to promotion." After Liu finished speaking, he designated Zhang Biguo to read the regulations of the New Life Movement Group. After reading, Gao Qi, the secretary of the political affairs office, read the articles of association and implementation methods of the Use of Domestic Goods Association. The meeting adjourned at 4:50 PM. (June 26th)

Songjiang: A Tragic Drowning While Swimming in the River

During the hot summer, children everywhere often gather to swim in the river. Yesterday (the 28th) afternoon, Xiangguan, the fifteen-year-old son of Kong Binghe, who lived in Baojia Bridge, and Wang Gansheng, an apprentice at Da Honglou, along with a Mr. Wang, were walking by the railway. Kong suddenly had the idea of bathing in a small ditch behind the ice factory next to the railway. His companions declined because they were not good swimmers, but Kong still jumped in. However, there was a well in that place, about a bamboo pole deep. After Xiangguan went into the water, he was not seen coming up again. Bubbles floated to the shore. The companions knew that a disaster had occurred and rushed back to inform his family, ordering people to retrieve him. He had already died.

Tax Police Arrest Salt Smugglers and Send Them to Court

Cai Fugen, Wang Decai, Wu Afu, and Wu Hegen, residents of the Eighteenth District of Huangqiao Township, pooled their funds and traveled together to smuggle salt, hoping to make a small profit. Yesterday morning, as they were each carrying salt and passing through the triangular street of Xiapu Pond, they were captured by the stationed tax police team. After a brief preliminary interrogation, they were escorted to the county court on the 29th to be dealt with according to the law.

Taicang: Head of the Defense Corps Assassinated

Ben Haishun, a Hunan native and head of the special defense corps in Fulu Township under the county, originally intended to resign and return to his hometown. However, just as he was about to leave, he fell ill. After recovering, he was burdened by economic hardship and unable to return home. Suddenly, the night before, he was assassinated. He suffered six knife wounds, and the flesh was a bloody mess, a tragic sight to behold. The murderer is at large and has not been apprehended, and the motive is unknown. After the incident, the Third Sub-bureau of Public Security found two carpenters' iron axes with bloodstains on them under the dirt behind the district office. It is suspected that they were the murder weapons and were immediately kept on file at the bureau. The county government commissioned Shen Cheng, an investigating officer, to go to the countryside to examine the body, ordered the local constable to prepare a coffin for burial.

Careless Launch of the Luwu Shuttle

The Luwu shuttle, which travels between Taicang and Luwu, caught fire on the morning of the 28th at around 10:00 AM. When it docked at the wharf outside the Great North Gate after arriving in Taicang from Lu, passengers disembarked, and the mechanic routinely added gasoline. However, due to a moment of carelessness, the gasoline caught fire and quickly spread throughout the ship. The attempt to extinguish the fire was unsuccessful, and the entire ship was reduced to ashes. The two mechanics, surnamed Zhou and Mao, were burned and have been rushed to Taicang Hospital for treatment. The losses are said to be enormous.

Changshu: Rice Prices Soar Amidst Severe Drought

Since the beginning of summer, the weather has been extremely hot. It has been even worse in the past four days. According to older people, this kind of extreme heat has not been seen in nearly twenty years. In addition, there has been no rain, and the rivers have dried up, making it impossible for farmers to draw water. The fields are cracked. In the higher fields, the rice seedlings have already turned yellow. Farmers are all worried. Even the wells of residents in the urban area are nearly dry. If there is no rain, there will be a major problem with drinking water. Therefore, there have been rituals for praying for rain in various places recently. Although the matter is superstitious, the authorities cannot prohibit it. Because of all this, rice merchants hoarding rice are taking advantage of this opportunity to raise rice prices. Yesterday, the ticket price for top-quality white rice reached more than nine yuan. Soon, it will exceed ten yuan. Poor people are extremely panicked.

Father and Son Both Die of Heatstroke

Wang Tonggen, a farmer in Qianjia Lane, Xitang Bridge, Fourth District, earns his living by farming. Recently, due to the severe drought, the fields needed a lot of water. Wang, under the scorching sun, worked hard to draw water with his son, Chaochao. Unexpectedly, due to excessive heat, both father and son suffered heatstroke and collapsed one after another, dying without rescue. It is said to be tragic.

Wuxi: More News About the Guard Corps Homicide Case

Han Zike, a member of the Shangshan Guard Corps in the Eighth District, shot himself and wounded the cook, Han Weibiao, in the abdomen. Han Zike died on the spot, while Han Weibiao was transported to Puren Hospital for treatment. Later, Prosecutor Shan Ren led officials to the countryside to investigate, confirming that Han Zike shot himself to death. The situation has already been reported in this newspaper. Now it is learned that Han Weibiao also died in the hospital due to his injuries. Yesterday, Jiang Xinfu, the squad leader of the guard corps, reported to the local branch court. Prosecutor Ren again led officials to investigate, determining that the bullet entered the abdomen and pierced diagonally towards the right waist, without exiting. However, the doctor had already performed surgery to clamp out the bullet. It was confirmed that he died from the gunshot wound he sustained while alive. After the investigation, the corpse's wife, Han Jinshi, was ordered to prepare a coffin for burial.

Changzhou: Telephonic Request to Protect Educational Funding Independence

The Wuyi County Education Association, in response to the Department of Finance's order to implement the measures for the collection, expenditure, and deposit of county funds in each county starting on July 1st, believes that it endangers the independence of educational funding. Therefore, yesterday (the 28th), it telegraphed the Provincial Government's Department of Education, stating that educational funding has special circumstances and is difficult to equate with other expenses. If the county treasury measures are implemented, there will be many obstacles. It requested that the spirit of joint consultation and independence be maintained and made three suggestions: (1) For the safekeeping of educational funding in each county, it is proposed to establish a county education funding management office, modeled after the provincial funding collection and expenditure measures. (2) The educational funding audit committee in each county should expand its powers to thoroughly review revenue and expenditure accounts. (3) The educational funding safekeeping plan in this province does not violate party guidelines or any laws and regulations, has been implemented for many years, and has been quite effective. It should be appropriately preserved to strengthen the foundation. As for the county funding collection, expenditure, and deposit measures that are suitable for use, they may also be adopted together to achieve perfection.

Zhenjiang: Construction Begins on Entire Zhenli Road

The Zhenli Road is of great importance. Currently, only the roadbeds and surfaces of the Zhenjiang and Liyang sections have been completed. The entire Jinli section of the road, including the Tanjing area, has not yet been started. It should be quickly constructed to complete the entire road for traffic. It has been found that the Zhenjiang section of the roadbed and surface construction has been approved for the Zhenjiang Danjinli Long-Distance Bus Company to handle through open bidding. All of the road surface engineering for that section must be completed by the end of June of this year. As for the Jinli section, the Construction Department has ordered the county to build it as soon as possible. The Zhenjiang section's roadbed construction has already been put out to bid by the company and construction commenced on the 8th of this month.

Short-Run Service Added Between Zhenjiang and Xin'an

Every year during the summer flood season along the Grand Canal, there is a shuttle boat running between Zhenjiang and Danyang, stopping at small towns such as Xinfeng, Jianbi, and Dantu. This year, the company is operating as usual. However, due to the shorter route, it runs from Xinfeng to Zhenjiang every morning and from Zhenjiang to Xinfeng at 3:00 PM every afternoon, providing convenience for local people.

Nantong: Police Chief of Haimen County Relieved and Sent to Province

Cheng Rusong, the police chief of Haimen County, was accused of protecting evildoers and releasing criminals to the Jiangsu Provincial Security Department. Director Xiang ordered Zheng, the special commissioner of the Nantong District, to order the Haimen County Government to suspend Cheng Rusong from his duties and send him to the province for interrogation. His vacancy was filled by Zhang Jing, the deputy commander of the Haimen County Defense Corps. Cheng Rusong was escorted from Hai to Tong and sent to Zhenjiang on the 28th. All circles in Haimen, because Cheng had been in Hai for six years and was loyal to his duties, sent representatives to Tong to petition the special commissioner. Commissioner Zheng promised to convey the local public opinion to the provincial office when he went to the province on the 29th. The representatives returned to Hai satisfied.

Student Military Training to Begin as Scheduled

Military training for students above the secondary level in Nantong will begin on July 1st and last for three weeks. The entire county will establish one large unit, with the district security commander concurrently serving as the general captain. Tongzhong will form one squadron, Chongzhong one squadron, and Tongyuan Affiliated High School and Tongshi will jointly form one squadron.

Local News

The Panchen Lama Advanced to the Capital Last Night, Mayor Wu and Others Went to the North Station to See Him Off, He Will Remain in the Capital Temporarily to Meet with Chairman Chiang

The National Government Commissioner, the Panchen Lama, has been warmly welcomed by all circles since arriving in Shanghai. The Lama is urgently required to advance to the Capital to discuss with the Central Government all the procedures for preparing to return to Tibet. It was originally scheduled to set out yesterday morning, but due to the hot weather, it was changed to 11:00 PM last night to travel to the Capital by night train.

Station Decoration

The Railway Bureau attached a large floral carriage to the night train yesterday for the Lama to ride in. The inside and outside of the car were covered with yellow silk. There were also two first and second class special cars and two luggage cars. A yellow silk archway was erected in front of the North Station gate, with the words "Farewell" written on it. The platform was also decorated with yellow lanterns. Military police were densely deployed inside and outside the station, and the Public Security Bureau's military band played music to see him off.

Farewell from All Circles

Those who went to the North Station last night to see him off included Mayor Wu, Section Chief Li Dazhao, Security Director Yang Hu, Executive Yuan Secretary-General Chu Minyi, Chen Jitang's representative Yang Dezhao, Yu Qiaqing, Wen Lanting, Qu Wenliu, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, Wang Xiaolai, and dozens of others. The Lama and his party arrived at the station at 10:45 PM, shook hands with the well-wishers one by one, and then boarded the floral carriage, leaving Shanghai amidst the military music.

Chu's Luncheon

Executive Yuan Secretary-General Chu Minyi came to Shanghai from the Capital yesterday morning and held a luncheon at his residence on Albert Road to bid farewell to the Lama. Mayor Wu and Xu Shiying were invited to accompany him. The guests and hosts enjoyed themselves until 2:00 PM.

Visiting Chairman Chiang

Last night at the station, Chu Minyi told the reporter of this newspaper that the Lama will stay in the Capital temporarily or go to Tangshan to avoid the heat. The date of his return to Tibet will be decided after thorough consultation with the Central Government. The Lama has not yet met with Chairman Chiang, so he plans to go to pay his respects when Chiang returns to the Capital. There is no intention to go north to Beiping to avoid the heat in the short term.

The Process of Through Train Negotiations, The Oriental Travel Service Does Not Establish a Branch in Shanghai

The much-talked-about through train issue has now been officially announced. Starting tomorrow, it will be officially implemented. It is rumored that there will be one train running in each direction between Beiping and Shenyang tomorrow, both of which are trial runs. Passengers will be officially carried starting on the 2nd. Yesterday, the reporter specially visited someone familiar with the process of the case. According to the discussion, the authorities were afraid that this issue might involve acknowledging the puppet Manchuria and were therefore very cautious from the beginning. Therefore, before the negotiations began, they approved three standard measures for through train service: (1) Limit one passenger train running in each direction per day. (2) The through train service will be undertaken by a commercial organization organized in accordance with Chinese law. (3) The commercial organization will liaise with the Railway Bureau on all accounts and business matters. After these standard measures were approved, a secret order was issued to the Political Affairs Reorganization Committee stationed in Beiping, instructing the Beining Railway Bureau to carefully negotiate with the Japanese side. The through train measures published in various newspapers yesterday were actually the result of the Beining Railway Bureau Chief Yin Tong's consultations with the Japanese side in accordance with the predetermined principles.

Another report states that the reporter inquired with the China Travel Service and was told by Chief Hua of the General Affairs Department that the price list and tickets for the Beiping-Shenyang through train have not yet arrived, so they cannot be sold. The director, Chen Xiangtao, has not received confirmation of when he will return to Shanghai. Another piece of information is that the train tickets and price lists for the Beiping-Shenyang through train will be sent to Shanghai today (30th). Starting tomorrow, China Travel Service and the Japan International Tourist Bureau will begin selling them. It is rumored that the Oriental Travel Service will not establish a branch in Shanghai. All matters will be handled by China Travel Service and the Japan Tourist Bureau.

Incident of Japanese Sailors Clashing with Western Police, Both Parties Conduct Thorough Investigation

The Great American Evening News says that the incident of the Japanese Marine Corps clashing with Western policemen on Zhapu Road will be thoroughly investigated by the Public Works Department and the Police Department. Although the details of the organization of the investigation committee are still unknown, it is said that it will pursue the truth, determine the responsibility, and begin processing it soon. After the investigation, a detailed statement will be issued by the Public Works Department. The Japanese Marine Corps will also send a representative to attend the investigation meeting as an observer. The Japanese authorities are still working to minimize the seriousness of this case.

The Continental News said that officials from the Public Works Department, the Police Department, and the Japanese Consulate remained silent yesterday regarding the clashes between the Japanese Marine Corps and Western policemen on Wednesday night and Thursday morning. Sterling Fessenden, director-general of the Public Works Department, told the Continental News reporter yesterday that Chief Inspector Joly had submitted a report, but did not comment further. The report is confidential, and the case has not yet begun to be investigated, as the Public Works Department is currently allowing the Japanese authorities to handle it. McNaughton, acting chairman of the Public Works Department, said that the Public Works Department did not want to comment on the case at this time. An official from the Japanese Consulate stated yesterday that the case is now in the hands of the Public Works Department, and the Public Works Department is currently conducting an investigation. An officer of the Japanese Special Marine Corps stated that the Japanese will attend the meeting to testify when the investigation is complete and indicated that no other steps have been taken. When the officer of the Japanese Special Marine Corps was interviewed by the Continental News reporter, he insisted that the Western police officer, Perami, had drawn his pistol and pointed it at the Japanese sailors. He also said that the reason for keeping Perami at the police station for six hours was to prevent him from going out and being injured by the crowd. He also said that in 1927, the Public Works Department had agreed with the Japanese authorities that patrolmen could not detain Japanese soldiers at the police station for questioning. When the case is investigated in the future, it is intended to present a letter signed by the chief inspector as evidence. Because of this agreement, he sincerely felt that the actions of the Japanese sailors on Wednesday night were justified. Now, looking at the overall situation of the case, the points of contention in this case are whether Perami actually drew his pistol, whether Perami was forcibly detained for six hours, and whether the Public Works Department had an agreement that patrolmen could not arrest Japanese soldiers at the police station in peacetime. According to the previous Sino-Japanese War, the Japanese authorities insisted that, due to the state of war, patrolmen in the concession could not arrest Japanese soldiers. At that time, the police station detained several Japanese ruffians who were disrupting public order, but after the Japanese authorities lodged a serious protest, they were released.

Chairman Gan, Zhu Shaoliang, Visited Li's Residence Yesterday to Offer Condolences Regarding Li Zhengzhong's Death in a Car Accident

Li Zhengzhong, a member of the Gansu Provincial Government Committee and concurrently Secretary-General, tragically died in a car accident in Lanzhou. Chairman Zhu Shaoliang of Gansu, upon receiving the telegram in Shanghai, was deeply saddened. Yesterday morning, he personally visited the Li residence in Shanghai to comfort the family. Details of the situation are recorded as follows:

Details of the Tragic Death Yesterday morning, Chairman Zhu received a telegram from all members of the Gansu Provincial Government, reporting the details of Li's tragic death. On the morning of the 27th, Li was on his way back from the airport after seeing off Supervisor Ji Liang when his car collided with another car while vying for road space. The entire car overturned. Those in the same car as Li included Tian Kunshan of the Gansu Provincial Party Committee, Yu Yong, Director of the Political Department of the First Army, and a Mr. Yang, a health technician from the Ministry of Interior, among others. Li suffered the most severe injuries and died instantly. The other three were also seriously injured and sent to the hospital for treatment.

The Encoffining Ceremony the Day Before Yesterday After Li's death, his body was placed in the Zuogong Ancestral Hall in Lanzhou. The encoffining ceremony was held at 4:00 PM the day before yesterday (the 28th). Chairman Zhu, upon hearing the news in Shanghai, was deeply saddened. Yesterday morning, he personally went to Li's residence at No. 6 Xiafei Fang, Xiafei Road in the French Concession to comfort Li's family. It is reported that Li left behind a wife, two sons, and four daughters. The eldest son is eleven years old, the second son is four years old, and the eldest daughter is only seventeen and studying in the senior division of Yunzhong Girls' School. In addition, there is also an unborn child. The entire family resides in Shanghai.

Brief Biography of Li Li Zhengzhong, styled Miantang, was a native of Minhou, Fujian. He was forty-four years old. He graduated from the first class of the Baoding Military Academy. In his early years, he engaged in revolution. He participated in the Kichu Campaign against Yuan Shikai and the Bingchen Constitutional Protection Movement. During the Bingchen Constitutional Protection Movement, he entered Sichuan by a circuitous route, assisting in Dai Kan's campaign, for which he was credited with meritorious service. Subsequently, he served as Commander of the Wuhan Military Police, Commander of the newly formed Second Division, Commander of the Supplementary Division of the 26th Division of the Eleventh Army, Chief of the Second Route Staff, Director of the Central District Compilation and Reorganization, and Counselor of the Military Advisory Council. He currently serves as a member of the Gansu Provincial Government Committee and concurrently as Chief of Staff of the Pacification Commissioner's Office.
