Shen Bao Wireless Weekly

Shortwave Predictions After Twenty Years

— Wang Fumin

Thinking back to twenty years ago, when shortwave radio was just becoming practical, most amateur operators were active below 200 meters. Of course, at that time, there was no wireless telephone, and even if there was, it would have been on longwave.

So, what new developments will there be in shortwave radio twenty years from now? You only need to look at the progress in recent years to be amazed. So, in twenty years, the amazing inventions described below will definitely be realized.

First to be mentioned is television. Every radio expert agrees that television cannot be separated from shortwave. In other words, television depends on shortwave for its development, and in the future, it may even develop on ultra-shortwave. ￣

Currently, the largest shortwave radio station only emits 400 kilowatts, which seems relatively small. Undoubtedly, in the future, radio stations will need to increase to over 1,000 kilowatts, and there will definitely be such stations using this large amount of power. Now, let's talk about the only drawback of shortwave, which is fading. In the future, we will definitely be able to find a way to eliminate it. A DX station, for example, 10,000 miles away, can be received as clearly as a local station using a two-tube radio. At that time, there will be no need to be ambitious and build ten-tube or fifteen-tube radios. A one-tube, two-tube, or at most three-tube radio will be enough for you to use a loudspeaker.

In the future, when broadcasting commercial and political affairs, the same program can be broadcast in three or four languages and on the same wavelength. Readers will definitely find this prediction strange, but didn't the Columbia Broadcasting System already broadcast both radio and television on the same wavelength a few years ago? In the future, if someone in a distant place can turn the selector switch on their radio and listen to the language they understand, for example, a British radio station broadcasts English, German, and Spanish at the same time, with four reporters broadcasting the same program. This means that in the future, shortwave will be international.

In the future, mail between Europe and America will be sent by a specially made aircraft in the stratosphere, taking only four to six hours to arrive. The aircraft will not carry passengers, only small packages of mail. The piloting, landing, and departure of the aircraft will all be controlled by shortwave radio, which is what is called radio telemechanics.

Furthermore, there will be radio printing of newspapers. The Radio Corporation of America claims that it has invented a method of directly transmitting telegrams using ultra-high frequency (Facsimile telegram delivery system), which eliminates the clumsy method of dots and dashes and directly transmits text. Therefore, from now on (or perhaps even now), we can send handwritten documents, signatures, etc., to distant places using a facsimile machine.

Radio newspapers (Radio newspaper) use almost the same principle as the facsimile machine, completely automatically, without any human intervention. The machine includes a shortwave radio and uses a clock to control its operation. For example, at 2:00 AM, after receiving a special facsimile signal, a roll of newspaper will start to turn on a stick. At the same time, there is a special mechanical device (containing a compressed air bottle and an ink bottle, both of which are controlled by a modulated electromagnet) that sprays ink like mist. Printing uses a duplex system, so both sides of the newspaper can be printed at the same time. When the signal is received, the paper slowly turns, and a machine, like a typewriter, moves back and forth, roughly several times a minute. Then, the text, photos, etc., are printed on the paper. Half an hour later, the newspaper is completely printed and automatically folded by the radio and placed on a shelf. Tomorrow morning, you can have a newspaper to read. Of course, the newspaper printed at that time will not be as big or as much as the current newspaper, only four or five pages of local news, important declarations, and valuable photos. The price will definitely be very cheap, not exceeding the current price of newspapers.

Quick Method for Testing Open Circuit of Low Frequency Transformer

— Li Yuanqing

If there is a malfunction in the radio 丨丨 noise or no sound at all, the first step is to check whether the voltage of each pole of the vacuum tube meets the specified value. The second thing to test is whether the coil of the low-frequency transformer (or speaker) is damaged. According to experience and facts, for damaged radios, the source of the problem is on the low-frequency transformer, accounting for almost 80% to 90%.

Usually, to test a low-frequency transformer, it is generally necessary to disassemble it first. Then use a stethoscope or voltmeter in series with a battery to measure it. This method is not only cumbersome but also very uneconomical in terms of time.

[丨>Output Input<丨]

The figure shows the most common wiring method of a low-frequency transformer in a radio. Whether the transformer is short-circuited or not, testing according to the following steps can save a lot of time.

(1) First, connect the positive terminal of the voltmeter to the plate (P) of the vacuum tube socket, and the negative terminal to the grid (G). (As shown in the figure) If the voltmeter shows no reading at this time, it proves that at least one coil (the secondary coil of T1 and the primary coil of T2) must be damaged.

(2) Next, change the negative terminal of the voltmeter (with the positive terminal still connected to P) to the negative terminal of the filament (F-) of the vacuum tube socket. If the voltmeter (in series with the primary coil of T2 and the B battery) shows no reading at this time, it proves that the primary coil of T2 is damaged.

(3) Finally, change the positive terminal of the voltmeter (with the negative terminal still connected to G) to the positive terminal of the filament (F+) of the vacuum tube socket. If the voltmeter (in series with the secondary coil of T1 and the C battery) shows no reading at this time, it proves that the secondary coil of T1 is damaged.

The primary coil of T1, the secondary coil of T2, and the speaker coil can all be tested using the above method.

During the test, if:

(1) Although the voltmeter has a reading, the pointer is constantly jumping, which is a sign that the coil is about to break. At this time, there will be noise in the speaker.

(2) Although the voltmeter has a reading, its value is not lower than the original B voltage or C voltage, which is because there is a short circuit inside the coil. At this time, there will be no sound in the speaker.

Radio Can Cure Diseases

— Zhou Linbao

Marconi is the inventor of radio. Many people know his name. According to recent news from Rome in the Western newspapers, this electrical genius, like Edison, is once again attempting to introduce radio into the medical field. He has invented the principle of using high-frequency shortwave radio to kill microorganisms in the patient's body. It raises the patient's body temperature to a level that is difficult for those microorganisms to survive, and they are all eliminated one by one. Although this method has not yet been tested on patients, if we think about how the mysterious radio was invented, then we can be confident that Marconi will succeed this time by a large margin.

There is also a new invention, an electrical scalpel for surgeons, which has the characteristic that the person undergoing the operation does not bleed. We may be a little doubtful when we hear this news, but it is true. It uses the force transmitted from a generator to immediately seal the blood vessels being cut during the incision, and no more blood flows out.

I want to bless this inventor for the people of the world, but the only hope is that when they are released to the world, they must not be as expensive as X-rays, so that the poor and sick can no longer afford to enjoy them!

Single-Tube Double-Effect Powerful Radio

— Liu Tongkang

Recently, single-tube loudspeaker radios have been very active in the radio world. Whether they are amateur or academic research comrades, almost everyone hopes to install one. The biggest advantage is that it is economical, simple, and effective. The radio that I am going to introduce now also meets the above principles.

The circuit of this machine was copied from a certain Western magazine. Because of the lack of materials, it was not possible to assemble it one by one according to the original circuit. I could only complete the machine by cutting corners. However, according to the test results, the performance is very good, similar to the effect of a two-tube machine using a No. 57 vacuum tube as a detector and a No. 56 vacuum tube as a low-frequency amplifier.

When testing at the beginning, the vacuum tube used was a No. 57, but later it was replaced with a No. 89 high-power output tube, and the effect was greatly increased. The volume was much louder than before, and the sound quality was also very clear and gentle.

The author of this machine is currently using it. The B battery is replaced with a substitute B battery, the output voltage is 180 volts, and the A battery is modified with a doorbell transformer, the voltage is 6.3 volts. Every evening, when using a loudspeaker to play music, all the major radio stations in Shanghai are received very clearly. Although the volume is not as good as an ordinary three-tube machine, it is more than enough to be heard in a room. This machine is very sensitive in selection. Under precise adjustment, the Oriental and Sino-Western radio stations, which are only 20 kilohertz apart, can be completely undisturbed. In addition, the reception range is also good, and Central, Japan, and Taipei can all be received.

In short, the effect of this machine is really not bad, and the circuit is simple, and the parts are very economical. General active comrades may wish to try it.

The circuit is shown in the figure: The vacuum tube V in the machine, the author uses No. 89, and others such as No. 57 and No. 77 can also be used, but the effect is worse!

C1 in the machine is a 0.00035 MFD variable capacitor for adjusting the wavelength, C2 is a 0.00025 MFD grid capacitor, C3 and C4 are both 1 MFD bypass capacitors, R1 is a 4 MEG grid leak, R2 is 1000, a fixed resistor, used as a substitute C battery, R3 is 100000, a potentiometer, used to adjust regeneration. T is a 5:1 low-frequency transformer, a 3:5:1 can also be used, and a 0.002 MFD fixed capacitor can be connected between the primary PB. RFC is a high-frequency choke coil to stabilize the oscillation, you can buy it ready-made or make it yourself. For self-made, you can use a temporary diameter tube and wind one or two hundred turns with No. 38 enameled wire.

The coils L1, L2, and L3 in the machine can use ordinary three- or four-way coils. The regeneration coil does not need to be rotated, or use three spider web plates, one winding 10 turns for L1, one winding 72 turns for L2, and one winding 35 turns for L3, all using No. 26 enameled wire. After winding, combine the three spider webs in one place and fix them in the machine. As for the positive and negative of the regeneration coil, it must be determined after testing.

Small Experience

(1) Utilization of Broken Bakelite Utensils and Records

— Yong Yan

Broken bakelite utensils and old or broken phonograph records are useless and like waste. They can be used as excellent insulators. Their use, of course, depends on the size and shape of the fragments; but within the possible range, they can also be artificially modified to suit the needs. For example, if you want to cut a large piece of broken bakelite or a record into a suitable small piece, you must first bake it with the flame of an alcohol lamp to soften it, and then cut it with scissors to the desired size and shape. It is also very easy to cut, no different from cutting cardboard. If you want to flatten an originally curved piece of broken bakelite into a flat plate; you must bake it soft with fire, and then gently press it with a wooden board, and it will become a flat bakelite board. The only thing to pay attention to during work is that the fire should not be too fast when baking, so as to avoid burning.

(2) Self-Made Method of Bakelite Tube

— Yong Yan

Bakelite tubes are imported and very expensive. They can also be made by yourself for application. Although the finished product is not as neat and beautiful as the purchased one, its function is the same, and it does not cost a penny. There is no difficulty in making it. Take a rectangular piece of broken record that has been cut into shape, bake it with fire to soften it, and then roll it on a round stick to make it round. After it cools and hardens, it is done. This method has a disadvantage, that is, there is a crack at the junction of the two ends; but this crack does not hinder the use.

(3) Lightning Arrester

— Wu Shanzhang

In summer, radios are always subjected to various threats, the most serious of which is high-voltage lightning in the sky. Therefore, those who have radios must install a lightning arrester. The price of those sold in ordinary electrical shops is always around one yuan, at least six or seven cents, and most of them are knife switches, and it is dangerous to forget to switch them off, which is very troublesome.

If we can pay a little attention, the materials for lightning arresters are everywhere, and the production is also very simple. Use two pieces of broken saw teeth, make their tips face each other, the closer the better, but not touching. One piece is connected to the antenna, then to the radio antenna post, and the other piece is connected to the ground wire, then to the ground wire post. Then, during thunderstorms, high-voltage static electricity in the sky will jump into the ground wire from the saw tooth tip, and the radio will not be damaged.

Similarly, carbon rods from small round batteries can be sharpened and placed opposite each other, and used pencil tips can be sharpened and placed opposite each other. However, pencils transmit electricity poorly.

(4) Substitute for Ground Wire Clip

— Wu Shanzhang

Those who live in Shanghai and have radios usually connect the ground wire to the tap water pipe because it is convenient and effective.

The substitute for the ground wire clip mentioned here is made of a folder. We connect the leather wire to the handle of the folder, and then clip the clip to the tap water switch. (You can't clip the pipe because the pipe is too thick)

Such a ground wire clip is very cheap.

[Ｐ>(5) Most Economical Key<Ｐ]

— Li Yuanqing

The cheapest key (Key) sold on the market also costs about two or three yuan. The one introduced in this article only costs a few cents to make.

Take a large wooden clothespin and screw it onto a wooden board, then install two screws on the tail end. (See attached figures A and B) When using, press the button. If you want to change the distance of the contact point, you can adjust the nut of screw A.

Spring and Autumn

Records of Imperial Incense in Misty Vapors

— Original by Princess Der Ling of Qing, translated by Qin Shouou

In the North, this dish has another name, called "Ringing Bell"; it is meant to describe how crisp it is, so crisp that people can chew out sounds. Therefore, this dish is always made as loose and crisp as possible, and the elderly can only sigh at it because of their incomplete teeth.

In the Empress Dowager's later years, cherry meat took the place of "Ringing Bell" and became the Empress Dowager's particularly favorite dish. The method of making it is to first cut high-quality pork into small pieces the size of chess pieces, add seasonings, and then mix it with fresh cherries, 丨丨 when there are no fresh cherries, put cherries that have already been candied or made by other methods in warm water to soak them, soaking them until they are as beautiful and tender as fresh ones. 丨丨 Together they are placed in a white porcelain jar, add some clear water, and let it simmer slowly over a low fire; after about ten hours, the meat is crispy, and the aroma of the cherries is also cooked out, so that greedy people can eat their fill at will. Especially the soup, it's really extremely delicious!

Among the several kinds of vegetables that are often eaten in the palace, the Empress Dowager liked "peas" the most. Peas are always picked when they are very tender, so not only is its taste very refreshing, but seeing its color, like green beads piled in a white porcelain bowl, it is also easy to arouse your appetite. Radishes were originally not qualified to be mixed into the imperial cuisine, because people in the palace have always been very dismissive of it, thinking that it is only food for the common people, or even used to feed livestock, and must never be used to desecrate the Empress Dowager; later, I don't know how, the Empress Dowager thought of it herself, and she ordered the eunuch in charge of the imperial kitchen to get some to try. Fortunately, those chefs were really smart, and with great difficulty, they managed to squeeze out all the original smell of the radish; then they paired it with ham soup or rich chicken and duck soup, and the taste would certainly not be bad!

The Legend of Suzhou's Xuanmiao Temple

— Nan Gong Sheng

When Suzhou's "Xuanmiao Temple" is mentioned, everyone knows it's a famous place in Suzhou. In reality, it's just like the City God Temple in Shanghai, a small general merchandise market. However, there are particularly many legends about the "Xuanmiao" Temple, the most famous being about the "Sanqing Hall," the "Wordless Stele," and the "Large Water Basin."

The "Sanqing Hall" is a large hall in the center of the "Xuanmiao Temple," where the true Three Pure Ones are enshrined: Lao Tzu, the Primordial Celestial Venerable, and the Master of the Heavens. The three statues are over ten zhang tall, their heads touching the roof beams, and their lotus pedestals are built directly on the ground, making them truly magnificent. The legends about the "Sanqing Hall" revolve around these three statues. It is said that in the beginning, there were only two statues in the "Sanqing Hall." The addition of the third statue was due to a spring eye located beneath its base. This spring eye was said to connect to the Eastern Seas. Therefore, the third statue was erected to rely on the spiritual power of the Three Pure Ones to鎮住 suppress the spring eye, otherwise, the entire city of Suzhou would be baptized by seawater. Hence, there is a saying, "If the Three Pure Buddhas fall, Suzhou City is done." Whether this is true or not is unknown since the Three Pure Buddhas have never fallen.

The "Wordless Stele" was erected by Liu Bowen to鎮住 suppress the feng shui of Suzhou City. Because the terrain of Taihu Lake is much higher than that of Suzhou City, without this "Wordless Stele," the water from Taihu Lake would flood the city, and the people of Suzhou would become fish and turtles. Due to this legend, the "Wordless Stele" still stands behind the "Sanqing Hall" and to the side of "Zhongshan Hall," and no one dares to touch it.

The "Large Water Basin" is also behind the "Sanqing Hall." It is said that there are two spring eyes in the "Xuanmiao Temple," one under the base of the Three Pure Buddhas and the other in the "Large Water Basin." Therefore, regardless of drought or flood, winter or summer, the water in the "Large Water Basin" has never dried up, which is solid proof of the spring eye connection. However, if you go to the "Xuanmiao Temple" now, you can see that the "Large Water Basin" is completely filled with bricks and earth, and there is no trace of any clear spring water. This legend has clearly become a thing of the past. As for the "Sanqing Hall" and the "Wordless Stele," one is because the statues are too tall and no one can move them, and the other is because the implications are too great and no one dares to try. Whether they conform to the legends is unknown.

Brain Surgery

— Luo Nu Xia

The other day, our international news reported: "Leningrad" Surgical Academy successfully performed a brain transplant. It is said: '::: A pigeon-egg-sized adenoma was removed from the brain of a young woman, because if the tumor grew larger, it would cause her to go blind. The location of the tumor was several millimeters from the central nerve. The surgeon, relying on his lifelong skills, was able to move the brain aside and remove the adenoma. This can be considered a groundbreaking event in the medical world," etc. In fact, the success of brain surgery did not begin today. Chinese novels have long recorded that during the Qianlong era of the Qing Dynasty, the scholar Qi Zhaonan broke his brain, and a doctor used horse brain to repair it for him. Although he did not die, he lost his intelligence and forgot everything he had previously read. This is one case.

I heard that twenty years ago in San Francisco, a young woman named "Jane Napa" committed theft and was arrested by the police. Her father was a wealthy businessman who bailed her out. Presumably, she suffered from a mental illness; otherwise, why would she be so muddled? He hired a famous doctor to treat her. After an examination, the doctor said: she damaged her brain in childhood, so rotten bones grew inside, hindering her original conscience, which is why she did things regardless of the consequences. Later, after the doctor dissected and repaired it, within ten days, the evil roots were removed. That is another case.

Combining these two cases with the so-called successful brain transplant now, one can only say that they "mutually complement each other."

Where Does This Debt Begin?

Old Debts of the Four Northeastern Provinces

The Shad of Fuchun and the Pine of Huangshan

— Da Kuai

People only admire the perch of Songjiang but rarely mention the shad of Fuchun. Only the "Remnants of Wulin Affairs" once recorded: "Every year in May, the shad fish on the Fuchun River are at their peak. The Huizhou people catch them and transport them hundreds of miles to the cities in a short time. Some say that this fish comes from the Han River and is not produced in Fuchun. Neither the upper nor the lower reaches of Fuchun have this fish except in summer, which people find strange." In fact, early summer is the spawning season of the shad, which come with the spring tides, and they become the delicacies of the Seven Mile Rapids. The Huizhou people passing through here never fail to enjoy a feast.

The fish is flat and long, the larger ones being over three chi long, with white color like silver, high in fat, and very delicious. However, the flesh has many fine bones and dies soon after leaving the water, and the taste diminishes when dead. Therefore, one must taste it on the boat. The boatmen of Huizhou are skilled at cooking this fish. Now that the automobile road is open, this flavor will probably be difficult to obtain. After a few more years, "eating shad in the Seven Mile Rapids" will probably become a story in the mouths of the elders.

With the opening of the Huizhou-Hangzhou Road, more and more people are traveling on Huangshan Mountain. The products of the mountain are favored by the elegant literati and reclusive scholars, which is very fortunate. Among the eastern tourists, the pine is the most popular. Between rattan boxes and walking sticks, there are verdant, delicate and small pines, all freshly uprooted from the mountains and brought to the human world. If the mountain spirit knows, how can it not be stingy?

In fact, the best pines are mostly on steep cliffs, making them extremely difficult to obtain. The next best are those growing on rocks, and the worst are those growing in mud. Most of what is sold are middle and lower grades. Some are artificially bent to make them crooked, which not only loses their natural appearance but also does not last long. The best pine needles are short, dense, and sharp (prickly), while ordinary leaves are double-stranded. It is said that there are three-stranded and five-stranded ones between Tian Du and Lianhua, but they are not easy to obtain.

To plant pines, one must use yellow mud and place them in a sunny place. Dryness is not a problem, but dampness is most avoided. During each metabolic period, the yellow leaves must be pruned to prevent them from falling off naturally. If they fall off naturally, the new growth will be... and the green and brown colors will be mixed, which is not aesthetically pleasing.

The Real Old Shanghai and Its Artists

— Shanghai Tongshe

"Controlling the rivers and gathering merchants from Huai and Zhejiang; connecting to the sea and facilitating transportation from Fujian and Chu; ::::: gathering people of different races in the city; trading goods from the southeast :::::"

The above quotations are two lines from the "Qinglong Town Ode" by the Song Dynasty poet Ying Xi. Even if the words of the ancients were exaggerated, let's discount it by half, and it is still 50% accurate. Then, this Qinglong Town seems to be quite extraordinary. But what exactly is Qinglong Town?

As it turns out, this Qinglong Town was actually old Shanghai.

Legend has it that Sun Quan of Wu once built Qinglong warships there, hence the name Qinglong. It was first established as a town in the fifth year of Tianbao in the Tang Dynasty (746). In the Song Dynasty, it belonged to Huating County. In the Yuan Dynasty, after Shanghai was established as a county, it was divided and belonged to Shanghai. In the Ming Dynasty, it belonged to Qingpu.

The local chronicles tell me the rough outline of this old Shanghai, and especially point out:

":::In the Song Dynasty, the town was a hub for seagoing ships, with three pavilions, seven pagodas, and thirteen temples, and ten thousand families with smoke, and people called it Little Hangzhou."

Old Shanghai also had the beautiful name of Little Hangzhou. It seems that although it did not have the momentary fame of the current Shanghai, which has earned the honor of "Paris of the East," there is no doubt that the Qinglong Town of old Shanghai was prosperous a thousand years ago.

It is said that there was a man from Qinglong Town named Li Jia, with the alias Jingyuan, who was skilled in painting and wrote good poetry and lyrics, and was praised by Su Dongpo. Dongpo once inscribed a poem on Li's magpie painting:

"I heard of the immortal Guo Zhongshu, whose drunken brushstrokes were magnificent. Where are the people who have been lonely for a hundred years? Only Li Jingyuan of Huating remains."

There was also a man named Li Wu regret, with the alias Xingzhong, who was not originally from Qinglong Town but lived in Qinglong Town. He lived a leisurely life, devoted himself to poetry and wine, and built an elegant garden. He did not hold office or receive stipends, but he was highly respected by the famous officials of that time. Su Dongpo inscribed the name "Drunken Sleep" on a pavilion in his garden and wrote a poem to him. Su Ziyou, Qin Shaoyou, Zhang Ziye, and others echoed with rhymes.

Mei Shengyu, a famous poet, often traveled to Qinglong Town. In addition to the "Qinglong Miscellaneous Records," he also wrote a poem "Watching the Tide on the Qinglong River," which reads in part:

"A hundred rivers converge, the water seems to stand upright, soon turning back as if sucked in by the nose. Old fish have no guard and go up and down, crying sadly towards the misty continent. ::: After years of nourishing a fatty body, it suddenly becomes food for the fishermen. Who can rely on the merciless water, which will easily sink them. :::"

The Qinglong River has long been buried, and the river tide is no longer seen. Now, the people of Shanghai have to go to Haining to watch the tide. We never imagined that we could discover the greatness of the ancient Qinglong River tide in the laments of this old poet.

There was also an official named Mi Fu, with the alias Yuanzhang, who served in Qinglong Town. Everyone knows that Mr. Mi's calligraphy and painting were admired by people of that time, now, and in the future. He left two valuable items in the old Shanghai area:

1. Record of the Sutra Collection of Longping Temple (calligraphy)

2. Picture of Shanghai South Scenery (painting)

These artists became the group of artists of old Shanghai in the local chronicles.

Free Talk

On the Construction of Mass Language

— Fan Zhongyun

Fifteen years of the vernacular movement, and now we hear calls for classical Chinese to rise again. Isn't this a strange thing? But no, in this era where mandarin jackets are becoming popular, this is exactly what we expected.

The vernacular movement was a post-war manifestation of Chinese national bourgeoisie demanding reform and the establishment of a modern China, influenced by the principle of national self-determination. However, this demand was immediately crushed under the immense pressure of international capitalism. Consequently, on one hand, the vernacular movement immediately became a movement to sort out national heritage; on the other hand, it merely transformed the feudal stories of talented scholars and beautiful ladies into descriptions of romances between modern men and women. The vernacular movement, after changing "之乎者也" to "的那吗呢", came to an end.

Therefore, this so-called vernacular is, in reality, not much different from classical Chinese. It not only failed to connect with the general public, but its fundamental consciousness remained the same as classical Chinese: feudal, pleasure-seeking, consumerist, and exploitative. Therefore, it goes without saying that this kind of vernacular needs to be reformed. But to avoid repeating past mistakes, the question arises. ㈠ is the issue of consciousness, pertaining to the expression of thought; ㈡ is the issue of knowledge, pertaining to the enrichment of content. I believe the issue of language is third, but these three must advance simultaneously for success to be achieved.

On the one hand, we need to make the vernacular a vivid language of the general public; on the other hand, the thoughts of the masses are still dominated by texts like "Yinzhiwen" and "Ganying Pian," and we need not shy away from admitting that their level of knowledge is low. In this respect, they are practically a blank slate. Therefore, we must input new knowledge to enrich their vocabulary and introduce new ideas to correct their consciousness. Once knowledge is enriched and thinking is correct, I believe the vernacular and the language of the masses will naturally converge.

Speaking of the dissemination of knowledge and the correction of thought, apart from textbooks, newspapers and magazines are the most important. However, today's textbooks, like the vernacular of the past, are often mere translations of classical Chinese, and current newspapers are filled with expressions of feudal consciousness. For example, when reporting on male-female issues, they say things like "The secret affair has been going on for a long time," or "A clandestine pregnancy results in a swollen belly." Other news often concerns individuals, such as "So-and-so departed from Beijing at such-and-such time by special train, seen off by So-and-so," or "Arrived at such-and-such place at such-and-such time, greeted by So-and-so," or "So-and-so association held a meeting at such-and-such place, attended by So-and-so." Rarely is the social significance of these events pointed out. In short: the formularization of news reporting is due to the deep poison of classical Chinese.

Therefore, although the vernacular movement has been around for fifteen years, the general public still lacks reading material. But since they have already learned to read, they want to read, and have no choice but to seek satisfaction in old novels such as "Water Margin" and "Dream of the Red Chamber," or to read things like "Tixiao Yinyuan" and martial arts novels, or, a little more modern, romance novels from "New Saturday." This low-level taste leads to the prevalence of tabloids and yellow journalism dominating the entire news industry.

Speaking of it, the formation of this phenomenon is still due to the premature end of the vernacular movement. Therefore, those engaged in cultural movements should know that we must first ensure that the general public has something to read. Only in this way can we cut off the remaining influence of classical Chinese and eliminate all the low-level tastes solidified by feudal consciousness of consumption and enjoyment.

To construct mass language literature, we demand reading materials that meet the needs of the masses.

Two Misconceptions

— Cao Juren

Mr. Wang Maozu, in discussing "Prohibiting the Study of Classical Chinese and Forcibly Requiring the Reading of Classics," feels that the writing level of the general youth is declining and that they must re-read classical Chinese and write in classical Chinese. Although Mr. Wang is said to be an educator, he is ultimately an amateur in the field of Chinese language teaching. Not only an amateur, but simply beating around the bush and utterly useless.

People who care about education often have two misconceptions: some forget their previous writing level and think that the writing level of modern youth is particularly low. Some forget the incomprehensible elements of classical Chinese writing and think that all incomprehensible elements come from learning vernacular Chinese. I will concede a step and admit that the general writing level is declining and that there are more incomprehensible elements in vernacular Chinese than in classical Chinese, but Mr. Wang's responsibility becomes even greater. Principals of secondary schools in various places tend to hire old-fashioned Chinese language teachers. Most hire so-called "venerable scholars," and those leaning towards the new tend to hire so-called "writers." How can a venerable scholar explain modern Chinese language textbooks? Not only can he not explain masterpieces like Maupassant's "Moonlight Night," but he is also bewildered by Huxley's "Evolution and Ethics." But when it comes to ancient books, their knowledge is limited. Their understanding of classics relies solely on Zhu Xi's commentaries, their knowledge of history is limited to Zuo Zhuan; their understanding of rhetoric and literary theory is even more superficial. Can these kinds of old-fashioned scholars instruct young people with correct knowledge of language and writing skills? As for the writers who are touted as being beautifully talented, their fame only spreads throughout China. Calling on them to teach Chinese language courses, they cannot explain the old and have no way to teach the new. I know of several writer-professors who simply spend time on the podium telling anecdotes and discussing current events. Can this improve the language level of young people? Chinese language teaching is the specialty of a teacher, and cannot be easily handled by three sermons and eight bushels of talent. Therefore, if young people have any shortcomings in language, it is the fault of the secondary school principals who wrongly hired Chinese language teachers. Mr. Wang Maozu is one of those who cannot escape responsibility.

As for the general language level of young people, that is beyond the knowledge of Mr. Wang Maozu. Let me use an analogy from the past to explain the present: Fang Bao and Yao Nai were masters of the Tongcheng School, and their prefaces and inscriptions were quite admirable; but when it came to matters of state, they were full of flaws. Their discussion of border defense affairs was simply a joke. I love Gui Youguang's writings the most, but his large-scale writings are not worth reading. Among the writers of the Tongcheng School, only Zeng Guofan's large-scale writings are pleasing to read. It can be seen that argumentative writing is related to experience and observation, and cannot be deeply observed until after middle age. If we use topics such as "The responsibilities of young people during times of national crisis" and "Reading without forgetting patriotism, patriotism without forgetting reading" to examine students' language level, there is nothing to say beyond platitudes, and it is naturally difficult to get satisfactory results. In fact, even if Fang Bao and Yao Nai were asked to submit papers on such topics within a limited time, they would not be able to write good articles. The national language test questions for university entrance in Europe are mostly practical topics such as "Morning Glow" and "Street," and they never focus on empty theories. (I saw a Chinese language test question on "On Propriety, Justice, Integrity, and Shame" at a certain middle school the other day. The use of the word "on" in this test question is incomprehensible; it should be "speak" or "meaning." If you ask Mr. Wang to write an essay on this topic, I dare say Mr. Wang may not be able to produce anything good.) Modern youth have a wider range of knowledge than in the past; all the subjects they learn cultivate organizational skills, so their language level is indeed much higher than that of previous literati. I have carefully studied this issue: the less ancient books one reads, the higher the language level; the more ancient books one reads, the lower the language level; if you don't believe me, you can test it in practice. (As for using the number of typos and the quality of handwriting as language standards, that's a different matter.)

There is also a common concept that misleads young people, which is what educators call "equal emphasis on Chinese, English, and mathematics." The level of language is directly proportional to the amount of common sense; as the ancients said, knowing people and discussing the times requires a rich knowledge of history, otherwise it is difficult to make sound arguments. Su Xun's "Six Kingdoms Theory" was once praised as a masterpiece, but from today's perspective, it is absurd and ridiculous; the fault of selling Yi Guo's abandonment has been passed down for thousands of years; in reality, there are many fallacies; this is all due to ignorance of historical events. To put it bluntly, the more equal the emphasis on Chinese, English, and mathematics, the less time young people have to take care of other subjects, the less common sense they lack, and therefore the more their language cannot progress; only by allowing them to gain more common sense and activate their thinking ability can there be hope for improving the language level.

News Reporter's Seat

— Er An

On Re-translation and Other Things (Part 1)

— Mu Mutian

In my old "Each According to Their Ability," I raised my opposition to re-translation.

There are indeed some bizarre facts in modern China. For example, isn't it still common in China for Dr. Liu Tingfang to translate Maeterlinck's plays from English translations? I think that people with a good command of English like Dr. Liu Tingfang should translate English and American literary works from English rather than translating Maeterlinck.

In my opinion, people with a good command of English should translate more English and American works, and not abandon their strengths to pursue their weaknesses by translating French literary works from English. Those who study French literature should translate more French literary works, and not indirectly translate English and American literature from French translations. In my opinion, it is necessary to directly translate the literature of England, America, France, and Japan. Naturally, Russian literature and German literature need to be translated from English and French, and there is no other way to translate the works of Spain, Italy, Poland, and other small nations except indirectly. In "Each According to Their Ability," when I said, "If there is no other choice, it is permissible," I was referring to the translation of the literature of Italy, Spain, Poland, and other countries.

Regarding indirect translation, we still have some points to pay attention to. First, is the issue of criticism of the translation. I translated Nevirov's "Tashkent" from a French version, but last year I saw a German version of the book that was almost twice as long as the French version. And Louis Sault's "War" seems to have had a large chapter deleted in the French translation. Also, in some Japanese translations, the Japanese language is not very smooth. Isn't this a noteworthy issue? Criticism of translations is very important. Mr. Ma Zongrong is now translating "Don Quixote" from a French translation. He has two French translations, but there are many differences between the two French translations. How can this be done without criticism? Last year, I read Mr. Shen Qiyu's translation of "The Development of European Literature." It was based on a relatively good Japanese translation, and Mr. Shen Qiyu's translation was also quite faithful. However, there were still some funny mistakes. For example, when discussing Vigny's "The Death of the Wolf," the Japanese translator transliterated the word "wolf" as "Woruku," probably treating it as a proper noun, and Mr. Shen Qiyu transliterated it as "A'erke" without criticism. When I first saw it, I was baffled and couldn't remember which of Vigny's works had this A'erke character. But when I looked at the following text, I realized it was the wolf (Loup). Who knew that this wolf, traveling to Russia, then to Japan, and finally to China, had become Mr. A'erke. This point is naturally the mistake of the Japanese translator. Special attention should be paid to the work of criticizing translations!

If the work of criticizing translations is not done, and the work of indirect translation is done carelessly, the result is flawed. For example, Wang Renshu's friend's "Sociological Theory of Art" (Oe) is harmful to society. Over the years, I know of no fewer than three or five people who wanted to directly translate Oe from the original text. Many of them are sound in language and literary cultivation, but once Wang Renshu's inferior translation comes out, even if there are good translations, there will not be much opportunity to publish them. (In my opinion, Mr. Wang Renshu still has a lot of talent, so he doesn't have to translate only the first half of that book from Inoue Isamu's Japanese translation.) However, it would be much better if it were based on a better Japanese translation (the translations of Onishi and Koho). In my opinion, we should try our best to promote direct translation, and when there is no other choice, indirect translation is necessary. However, we must act cautiously, and it is best to base it on translations in more than two languages. And when there is really no other choice, it is possible to talk about flexible methods.

Old Goods Rehashed Biography

— Hong Liao

From a certain period onwards, the second-hand stores in Shanghai, quite catering to the preferences of the world, suddenly prospered. I have many friends who are regulars in some second-hand stores. According to their experience running second-hand stores, it is: although there are bargains to be had, after all, the quality of the goods is not as good as new ones.

Second-hand stores specialize in rehashing old goods and selling them at low prices to deceive people; many people flock to them in order to be greedy for small profits. Of course, this also contains elements of the urban recession. But the prosperity of rehashing old goods is not a good phenomenon, but has become a self-evident truth.

Opening our eyes and looking at our literary scene, isn't the trend of rehashing old goods developing in secret? Is this a good phenomenon?

Occasionally reading "Laozi" and "I Ching," one compiles some words that one doesn't even understand the meaning of into articles and sells them to young people who have never read ancient books: reciting Nalan Ci and Ding'an poems, one also writes a large number of post-reading feelings, or even forcibly inserts one's own consciousness, this is one. Reading "Dream of the Red Chamber," "Water Margin," or "Yesou Baoyan," one also forcibly cuts and renders a section of the content, becoming a new creation, this is two. In addition, such as reprinting ancient books, adding punctuation, and attaching eight-legged essay-style annotations. In this way, everyone is eagerly engaged in the work of rehashing old goods, thinking that this is a new trick to open up a new path. But is this really urgent work?

During the May Fourth Literary Revolution, the literary scene was flourishing, the promotion of vernacular Chinese, the overthrow of old poetry, this new literary movement had received the warm support of many young people. Now, how far is this work of rehashing old goods from the spirit of the May Fourth Literary Revolution? After September 18th, followed by January 28th, the country was in great difficulty; the literary scene also showed signs of decline, which is no different from everyone abandoning real life and running towards the grave!

Some people read books with a hobby as a starting point (because I fundamentally oppose reading for food, or reading for fame and fortune, etc.). We cannot force the hobbies of others, so we cannot forcibly prohibit other individuals from browsing and researching valuable old literature, or old books that are only for entertainment. But after browsing and researching personal hobbies, why bother to promote them widely? Is writing post-reading feelings about poetry and lyrics, or introducing the secluded writings of ancient novels, the literary cultivation needed by modern youth? Real life has prepared for us how many materials that can be used for literary and artistic creation. Why do some writers abandon reality and insist on running to the path of emptiness?

The work of rehashing old goods exposes the lack of real-life experience of writers, and thus takes the shortcut of expropriation in this way of avoiding the important and taking the light. This is the result of the recession, just like the prosperity of second-hand stores.

The rehashing of old goods in the literary scene can lure young people into old paper piles and forget reality. In order to save the decline of the literary scene, we should eliminate this work of avoiding the important and taking the light and escaping reality. What we need is something that is full of the spirit of the times and creation!

Elopement (4)

— Written by Petőfi of Hungary, translated by Shi Yongyi

Six months after Mrs. Anna and her nephew Karl eloped, a young man suddenly appeared at the home of old Andrew. His face showed an expression of suffering and disappointment.

Old Andrew had just returned from his club with a sad heart. He was grieving over the disappearance of his young wife and his failed chess game with the pastor.

When the young man came in, the old man, his face pale and trembling, collapsed into his chair. The young man took his hand and pleaded:

"Uncle! Dear Uncle! How can I get your forgiveness? I am prepared to follow your solution!"

"Where is she? That woman?"

"She... She... is not here."

The old man sighed deeply with relief.

"I want to tell you the whole story," Karl said. "Look, you should pity me, don't think of me as an enemy. I can't tell you how much I suffered. My happiness did not last long, I lived in a real hell, your wife has an angel's face... but her heart hides all the malice. She is the worst woman I have ever known. I can't live with her anymore... I have abandoned her..."

"My poor nephew... I have to sincerely pity you. But you should also pity me: you have only lived with her for six months, while I have lived with her for a whole year."

"You are also in pain, dear uncle?"

"I think you find it strange, don't you? Everyone thinks we are happy. But when we lived together, you should have seen it, then... you must have known one or two things. Just thinking of her makes me tremble. When I knew you had run away with her, I thanked you, no one has treated me more kindly than you. In order to reward you... when a merchant came to tell me your whereabouts... so I give you an annual subsidy... this way you can stop thinking about coming back and not have economic difficulties..." (The End)

Night Fishing

— Wu Wen

Night, the moonlit harbor, my wife counts the fishing lights on the opposite shore. One light, two lights... In the reeds. Clinging to phosphorescent light like soybeans. The still water suddenly ripples with silver snakes, and the two of us work together to haul up a layered net. A pointed, knife-like fish leaps and lightly slips away. Disappointment has become a habit, thankfully my wife is rushing to weave a new net. The child under the black awning is crying, my wife leaves me alone to guard the hatch. A breeze rises, the midnight tide rises, and the sound of fish leaping comes from the next boat.

Shen Bao This Local Supplement

Talk

Classical Chinese, Vernacular Chinese, Mass Language

— Bai Xi

First, we must pay attention to the reason why we are currently advocating the construction of Mass Language and discarding Classical Chinese and Vernacular Chinese, because the Vernacular Chinese Movement of the Hu Shi era did not actively discard Classical Chinese completely. On the contrary, it colluded with Classical Chinese and implemented a compromise. Therefore, it is inevitable to discard both Classical Chinese and Vernacular Chinese in providing for the construction of Mass Language at present.

Second, we must pay attention to the reason why we want to abandon Vernacular Chinese in the midst of opposing the revival of Classical Chinese, because, first, since Vernacular Chinese has compromised with Classical Chinese, of course, the quality contained in this Vernacular Chinese is no longer the pure quality of Vernacular Chinese. It has become a "hybrid" that is neither Classical Chinese nor Vernacular Chinese. Second, since Vernacular Chinese is compromising with Classical Chinese and stagnating, while the lives of the masses are advancing rapidly due to the promotion of the times, of course, the hybrid Vernacular Chinese does not match the current lives of the masses. It is inevitable to display Vernacular Chinese in the historical museum.

Third, we must pay attention to the fact that our advocacy of Mass Language must "use local dialects as much as possible to connect them into writing," because "dialects" and modern Chinese Mandarin (see Mr. Meng Ke's words quoted by Mr. Song Yang in the Free Talk of Shen Bao on June 26th (note that modern Chinese Mandarin is Mass Language)) although mutually opposed, can also penetrate each other under certain conditions. In order to "improve the modern Chinese Mandarin" as a whole, it is necessary to improve various "dialects" first. When various "dialects" develop to a certain extent, they can penetrate each other and become "modern Chinese Mandarin." I think this can relieve Mr. Goufo and Mr. Meng Ke of some doubts.

Fourth, we must pay attention to the fact that we are currently advocating the construction of Mass Language, and therefore want to discard (I think discard is more appropriate than overthrow) Classical Chinese and Vernacular Chinese, and those who "lump" Classical Chinese and Vernacular Chinese "together" as Mr. Goufo said, because Vernacular Chinese has compromised with Classical Chinese. Of course, since Vernacular Chinese is discarded, it is inevitable to discard Classical Chinese at the same time, so this does not make readers "dazzled and speechless." We know that the May Fourth Revolution did not completely eradicate all the feudal remnants! ...

The above four points were written after reading Mr. Goufo's "Declaration of War on Classical Chinese and Vernacular Chinese" published in Talk in yesterday's issue. I hope everyone will discuss it in twenty-four minutes so that this issue can be expanded and a perfect conclusion can be reached.

Mass Language

— Run Feng

I just learned that Mass Language must come from the working class, so yesterday I took a rickshaw to the factory area of Yangshupu to interview Mass Language, because I didn't know what kind of language Mass Language was. As soon as I stepped into the ×× factory, I immediately saw two working-class friends talking. As if I had found a treasure, I immediately walked up to them and stood by, listening quietly to their conversation. The words they said are recorded as follows.

A said, "Old San! Damn it, yesterday (pronounced "re," the following will be similar) Little Jiangbei came to my house to beg for blood. I said, 'Old Master, spare me! These (meaning this) few days, my pockets are empty. I'm thinking about finding a few friends and begging for some blood to use. What are you borrowing from me?'"

Little Jiangbei replied to me, "Damn it! You have to be prettier! We'll always run into each other in the future. Coming to your house to beg for blood today is still thinking highly of you. I don't know you, dog! I recognize you!"

"Old San! Think about it for me, aren't you angry? These few days, my blood is really all gone. Even if he wants to beg for some blood at my house, he should be more polite. I'm not going to give him anything."

B said, "Brother Six! Damn it! Don't say it, Jiangbei's thieving temper is always like that. Last year, he also came to my house to beg for blood, and his face was like a slow-moving master. I scolded him once, and he never came again. Later, when he saw me, he always turned his head and pretended not to see me. Damn it! I wouldn't bother with him either. I'm afraid of him doing something."

"Tonight, let's have tea at Xinminlou."

What About the Approaching Summer Vacation? | Presented to Student Readers |

— Wen Bing

Time flies like an arrow, and the summer vacation is almost here! We teachers and staff are anxiously worried about our jobs, while the students are all beaming with joy, jumping for joy. In China, this seems to have become a historical footnote, where all vacations are for playing, and "vacation" is synonymous with "days of play." Now, with the heat pressing down and the temperature soaring above 100 degrees, everyone is undoubtedly looking forward to the arrival of the summer vacation for a comfortable rest.

We not only oppose this, but also feel a deep sense of unease. Frankly speaking, this clearly reveals a weakness in the Chinese national character: seeking leisure and laziness. We know that students are young, energetic, and full of vigor. How can they just focus on seeking leisure and laziness? Looking at it from all angles, most people who serve society don't have summer or winter vacations. The laborers in factories who toil day and night, year after year, don't even know what a summer vacation is called (unless it's long-term unemployment, but even then they have to struggle to survive). Is it really so unbearable for us students to have only three to five hours of classes a day for just four months that we need a long period of rest? No matter how you say it, it just doesn't make sense.

We believe that summer or winter vacations during the academic year are merely an end to classroom learning, just a marker of the length of time, and not a time for everyone to play. We don't use grand excuses like "the nation is in crisis" and everyone needs to "endure hardship and strive for revenge." We are just telling the truth based on facts: summer vacation is not for us to play. We students don't need to play. We should strive for academic research, cultivate our minds and bodies, understand society, and plan for the future. In the vocabulary of students, there should only be "effort" and "progress," and not "laziness" or "rest." This is what we should deeply recognize.

Now that the general premise has been established, let's develop the following arguments.

Because education is not widespread in China, and because China's land is vast and transportation is inconvenient, the existing schools are all located in major cities and towns. In the countryside, apart from incomplete primary schools, you can't find universities or middle schools. Although schools are located in cities, there are not many students in the cities. Most of them still come from the countryside. Because of this, I want to propose a slogan: during the summer vacation, students should "return to the countryside"! I'm not just making a general argument here, asking students to shoulder the responsibility of revitalizing the countryside. Instead, I'm calling on students to go to the countryside to further their studies. The outline is as follows:

(1) The study environment in the countryside is good. We know that,

Page 22

Cities are densely populated, societies are complex, and everywhere is noisy and chaotic, with temptations and constraints. They are not at all suitable for young students to study hard. Only the countryside is pure, simple, quiet, and pleasant. That's why great philosophers like Rousseau strongly advocated returning to nature. Students should take advantage of the opportunity to leave school during the summer vacation and return to the countryside. They should follow the beautiful natural environment and strive to improve their studies.

(2) Go and understand the real society. Now it seems that everyone is saying that China has reached a point of crisis, and the most dangerous thing is the fundamental bankruptcy of the countryside. However, I think that everyone can probably only say this. No one is very clear about how bankrupt the countryside actually is, or what the real truth of society is. Especially students, who eat well, dress well, and sleep soundly at night, are just like palace maids in deep courtyards, worms in drums, and have no understanding of everything in society. Because of this, they naturally don't know how to work hard when they are studying, and they don't know how to seek transformation after they leave school. The summer vacation is a very good opportunity for us to go to the countryside and understand the reality of society. Moreover, in education, we can say that society is a university, and the knowledge we gain from this university is more valuable.

(3) See the hard work of parents and the difficulty of the source of tuition. Today's general students, once they leave their families, become vague and unclear. In school, they only worry about economic difficulties, not having enough money, and some students even complain about their parents. How inappropriate this is! Parents should of course bear the cost of their children's education, but children should also be thrifty to repay them, especially they should have a special understanding of their parents. See how hard parents work in the countryside, working tirelessly, saving every penny. In this time of rural bankruptcy, how difficult it is to raise tuition fees. Students should return home during the summer vacation to conduct a thorough investigation.

I personally strongly advocate that students return to their hometowns during the summer vacation.

The benefits gained, whether in terms of knowledge, physical and mental well-being, or understanding, are immeasurable. If, due to special circumstances, you cannot return to your hometown, you should also use this long summer vacation to go to the library and work hard, and go to factories or slums to do more practical social investigations. If you just eat your fill every day and play recklessly, or sleep in bed all day, that is absolutely inappropriate. As for detailed plans, how to use and allocate time, that is everyone's own business, and I won't elaborate further. In fact, it's useless to come up with them.

Confidence and Success

— Tian An

"Things must be rotten before worms grow in them..." This kind of old saying, although humble and not a great theory, also expresses a part of the truth. If a person is at odds with himself and willingly degrades himself, it is extremely difficult to hope to gain the respect and sympathy of others. This is exactly what is called "you reap what you sow," and you can't blame anyone. It's a pity that a good life is wasted in vain, which is too unworthy.

Success and failure in life, whether an individual strives to improve or not, has a decisive significance. In childhood, people are like a blank sheet of paper, dyed blue or yellow. They cannot realize their true position and often treat others as themselves, such as taking other people's opinions as their own. Children often lack confidence and always emphasize their weakness, willingly acting as appendages to their parents and elders. This is a necessary stage in physical development, and we cannot therefore say that children do not seek progress and deny their great future. In fact, the increase in age gradually enriches their physical appearance and also strengthens their inner spirit, especially the spirit of self-confidence, which develops rapidly. Of course, there are exceptions. We only need to see that many adults also lack confidence like children and live a weak and sad life, and it is not difficult to understand.

Our social status is different from that of children and is determined by ourselves. There are many "molds" in society that want to shape us into all kinds of people, and we have the right to choose. People cannot arbitrarily mold us into bad guys, nor can they mold us into sages. We have the right to mold ourselves into whatever kind of person we want to be. We can go up, or we can go down, depending on the degree of our confidence. Confidence often determines whether a person can succeed or not. Confidence is often a prerequisite for success and the driving force for courage and action.

This makes it necessary for us to have a new definition of our attitude towards life. For a person who is full of confidence and wants to work hard to improve, how should he handle his life in society? Will he be arrogant? Will he put on airs? Like many people with confidence? This is a dead end, and everyone can see its danger. Then, will he always have a series of humble words such as "You're old!", "I dare not!", "I am...", and say polite words? This is a spineless, soft performance and a prelude to the failure of people who lack confidence. He will be despised by others. He seems to be very polite, but there must be a limit to politeness, that is, politeness and humility must have a limit. Being too polite and too humble is not good. He cannot lose his independent and self-respecting position. As the saying goes, "A gentleman respects himself." A person with confidence does not necessarily have to be a feudal gentleman, but "self-respect" is an immutable principle for living in the world. Only by respecting yourself and looking up to yourself can you gain the respect and recognition of others. A person who lacks an independent and self-respecting personality will inevitably be looked down upon by others, such as servants, prostitutes, etc. Confidence, and the self-esteem and self-respect that arise from confidence, are the signposts on the road to success!

Remember! Only if you look up to yourself, will others look up to you!

Treasure

— Zhong Shuo

The weather was gloomy, the sky was full of fog, and the wind sounded like a threat, somewhat piercing.

Cai Bao, the landlord's servant, got up. His face was gloomy, and a worried expression was revealed. He squatted on the ground, watching Cai Bao's wife flipping through clothes one by one. Every time she turned to a more valuable piece of clothing, she hesitated for a while.

"The grain price is so low! The rent is heavier every year! The remaining coarse grains from last year were only finished last month. This is considered thrifty enough, but what can we do if God wants to abandon people!" Cai Bao spat out a few usual complaints.

Cai Bao's wife wrapped the more valuable clothes together. After hearing these words, she just sighed "Alas."

Cai Bao was about to leave, when Cai Bao's wife picked up a brand new cotton-padded jacket made of local cloth that had been worn two or three times, and said gloomily:

"Take this too!"

"Leave it behind! It's a pity to wrap up something new!"

"Can hunger be tied down? It would be better to take it to pawn for more money!"

Cai Bao unwrapped the package, and couldn't help feeling a pang of sadness. He remembered that when the rice ran out for the first time last month, he had pawned all of his wife's dowry clothes from the year before, leaving only this cotton-padded jacket. But now, it still can't escape this fate!

Cai Bao took the cotton-padded jacket. Suddenly, it felt like a knife point was grabbing his heart, and tears streamed down.

"Go quickly!" Cai Bao's wife sobbed.

Cai Bao wiped away his tears with his sleeve, sighed slowly, raised his head, and walked away. The needle-like northwest wind outside was getting stronger and stronger, hitting his face. His body heat, blown by this wind, felt like falling into an ice cave, and his heart couldn't help but tremble. "How can I be so useless!" When this thought turned in his mind, he gritted his teeth, straightened his chest, and walked on.

Page 23

On the Desire for Beauty

— 𠆩 Ting

The love of beauty is a human instinct. In our daily life and behavior, we often see manifestations of this desire. For example, loving to wear beautiful clothes, loving to eat palatable food, loving to live in elegant houses, loving to walk on quiet and clean paths, loving to see pleasing things, loving to hear interesting stories: these are all manifestations of the desire for beauty.

However, on the other hand, some people also say that life is about loving ugliness, the so-called evil desire. They say: Because we often see manifestations of human evil desires, such as: loving to kill, loving to invade, loving to harm natural creatures, loving to do things that benefit oneself and harm others. In this world, we have encountered many, many such facts.

So, do people love beauty or ugliness? Needless to say, people love beauty, because the love of beauty is a human instinct. The reason why people have evil desires is because the environment is bad, in other words, because they are people who are active under such a system.

Therefore, in order to wash away the existence of that kind of ugly concept in the world and fight against the desire for beauty, I think it is necessary to talk about it.

As mentioned above, the desire for beauty is a kind of desire for beauty, like the desire for food and the desire for sex. Of course, human thinking is complex, and there are many desires, not just the desire for beauty. For example, the desire for profit, the desire for knowledge, the desire for morality, the desire for survival, the desire for food, the desire for sex, etc. But the desire for beauty is one of the most important desires in life. Without the desire for beauty, what kind of ugly animals would humans become!

Therefore, some people say: "Truth, Beauty, and Goodness" are the three major elements of life.

So what is "Truth"? The pursuit of truth is a desire for knowledge, and the object of the pursuit of truth is science, because the origin of science is explained by knowledge.

What about "Goodness"? The pursuit of goodness is a desire for morality, and the object of the pursuit of goodness is morality, because the origin of morality is based on human behavior. Therefore, humans have measured present behavior through standards.

As for "Beauty"? The pursuit of beauty is naturally a desire for beauty, and the object of the pursuit of beauty is art, because the origin of art starts from human instinct.

Therefore, the main requirement generated by the desire for beauty is art, and art is one of the most valuable and meaningful things for mankind.

Therefore, we can say that the pursuit of beauty is a driving force for advancing life towards ideals. In order to change the form of human life and ugly concepts, the pursuit of beauty is a force that forms this new life.

Yearning

— Cun Yin

Xiangtan, my hometown.

There, I have my father and mother. There is also a younger brother and sister.

On a morning before the sun had risen, my father held my brother and carried a small suitcase. I carried the luggage. My mother held my sister.

Five people. Only four people's feet stepped on the hot dirt road.

There were no words on the road. Because we had already said a lot last night.

When we arrived at the pier, the sun had already climbed over the top of the mountain. It scorched all our sweat out.

We got on the boat.

In the cabin, we bought a berth from the tea room.

My father and mother's eyes were full of tears.

"Yin, when you get to Hankou, take the boat to Shanghai. There, your uncles are waiting for you!"

My father said with concern.

"Yin'er, you should take care of yourself on the road!"

My brother and sister both stared at me. These passionate eyes made my tears drip uncontrollably.

"Father, Mother. You should rest assured. Your child will definitely..." I sobbed.

My brother secretly tugged at my clothes and said.

"Brother. You must come back sooner!"

I suppressed some bitter smiles from my sadness and put them on my face, nodding to him.

"The boat is leaving!" "The boat is leaving!"

These sounds were like a sharp steel arrow. It struck my heart.

Everyone lowered their heads and couldn't speak.

Finally, I said to them, "Goodbye!" and bowed three times.

Quickly, they walked onto the pontoon boat.

The boat moved slowly.

I leaned on the railing and carefully watched the four faces.

Just as their four figures were about to become unclear, I took out a handkerchief and waved it at them.

In the distance, a little child was also waving.

"They must still be looking at me!"

I thought. My hand waved more and more tightly.

The boat accelerated mercilessly, and that side had turned into a white expanse.

Now, this has been five years ago! However, I still seem to be waving a handkerchief at them.

Xiangtan, my hometown, here is a fallen person, kissing your name!

The Deformed Society and the Contradictory City

— Yi Tong

Humble pursuits and base actions can lead to immense wealth! Loyalty and integrity often mean being penniless!

Correspondence Column

Workers' Supplementary Education Teacher

Dear Editor:

I am a female worker who sells her labor in a pharmaceutical factory. This pharmaceutical factory itself has many contradictions, and it uses special methods to oppress the workers. The contradictions are its own business, and we don't need to worry about it, but the oppression is our own pain, so we have to write it out and appeal to the public for help.

We sell ten hours of labor, but what do we get in return? Thirty cents a day, plus the mockery and abuse of the managers. This is a common phenomenon in general factories, and I don't need to be surprised and point it out in detail, but our factory director is different from others. He has come up with an incredible way to oppress us for both fame and fortune. He runs a night school and forces us to study. Others will definitely think that the factory director is very kind and is actually benefiting the workers by giving them supplementary education. In fact, ivory doesn't grow from a dog's mouth, and he doesn't have such intentions. It is because there are many drug names, so he forces us to attend night classes for one hour every day, teaching us to memorize X brand soda, X brand Marphinac, etc. There is nothing else besides this. Can this be considered supplementary education? Especially that slave-like teacher, who gets money from the factory and becomes arrogant, oppressing and humiliating us in every way (especially the young girls). Under this tyrannical power, we can only go to the toilet and cry.

Because the hot summer has arrived, the journey back home is already exhausting, and in addition, we have to do some personal chores: we have to eat, bathe, wash clothes, and those with children have to raise them. It is really impossible for us to go to school again. Therefore, many people don't go, and some people ask to study outside the factory. Who knows that the factory, which doesn't care about the lives of others, issued a decree: those who don't attend classes will be fired, and those who study outside will be fired. Should we attend classes this late? God, is our suffering brought out of our mother's womb? Isn't it enough for us to leave our families and sell ten hours of labor and sweat?

Because I live far away (more than five miles away), I have not attended night classes once, but I have been fired because of this. Several others have also been fired in the same way. We are going to be tortured by life again. Please, kind people who care about the people's livelihood, come and rescue us! Best regards,

Sincerely, Xu Man

Dear Editor, I am a friend of the female worker. Because she doesn't write very well, I ask you to be a ghostwriter. But mistakes are inevitable, please correct them and publish them. Ghostwriter's postscript

Editor's note: Improving the skills of the average person who will rely on wages to eat, so that their productivity is increased, and therefore the people who employ their labor are more profitable than employing uneducated people. In this society, the purpose of education is originally like this. The so-called supplementary education in Xu Jun's factory is just a very clear ironclad proof of this fact. Xu Jun is unemployed, and his current problem is to find another job. The motivation for writing the letter is probably that he is too angry, not that he wants me to discuss with him what attitude to take towards this kind of education, so I will not say how to deal with the factory. However, I think that the workers of the factory should unanimously demand the factory to cancel this kind of school, otherwise, this kind of learning should also be regarded as a part of the work, and the factory must also pay wages. This requirement is very reasonable.
